401 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Joseph


AC 36908


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


161 Conn. App. 850; 129 A.3d 183; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 480


September 24, 2015, Argued 
December 22, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Joseph, 320 Conn. 923, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 64 (Conn., Mar. 2, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault of a correction officer and possession of a dangerous instrument in a correctional institution, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, where the court, Newson, J., denied the defendant's motion to present a defense of necessity; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Strackbein, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of assault of a correction officer and the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the charge of possession of a dangerous instrument in a correctional institution; judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's appeal did not meet the requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a because it was not taken from the judgment of conviction following the denial of a motion to dismiss or a motion to suppress; [2]-The sole basis for appeal was that the trial court improperly denied defendant's motion to present the defense of necessity, but the trial court never made the mandatory finding that the denial of that motion was dispositive of the case, and the appellate court would not review defendant's claim on appeal in the absence of such a determination; [3]-The appellate court declined to review defendant's claim that the trial court improperly denied his request to pursue the defense of necessity because he failed to establish good cause; [4]-The issue he raised in the appeal did not transcend his particular case.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

 

402 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. City of Hartford


AC 36360


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


160 Conn. App. 677; 127 A.3d 278; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 404


May 18, 2015, Argued 
October 27, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Brown v. City of Hartford, 320 Conn. 911, 128 A.3d 954, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 437 (Conn., Dec. 23, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendant's alleged violation of the plaintiff's due process rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Robaina, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to disqualify; thereafter, the court, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee, denied the plaintiff's claim for a jury trial and the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Brown v. City of Hartford, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2593 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 12, 2013)
Brown v. City of Hartford, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1858 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 16, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that plaintiff could not prevail on his claim that the subject city ordinance was unconstitutional because it did not provide a post-deprivation hearing or other means to challenge the city's demolition of his property as the trial court properly determined, on the basis of well established precedent, that, under the emergency circumstances of the case where it was impractical for the city to provide any meaningful pre-deprivation due process to plaintiff, plaintiff's suit against the city provided him with a meaningful post-depivation hearing in which to obtain judicial review of the propriety of the city's actions and protected his constitutional right to due process.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

403 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Acker


AC 36578


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


160 Conn. App. 734; 125 A.3d 1057; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 399


February 5, 2015, Argued 
October 27, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Acker, 320 Conn. 915, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 22 (Conn., Jan. 20, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with sixty-three counts of the crime of cruelty to animals, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, geographical area number eighteen, and tried to the court, Danaher, J.; judgment of guilty of fifteen counts of cruelty to animals, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Acker, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 88 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 13, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted of multiple counts of animal cruelty, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-247(a) (amended). HOLDINGS: [1]-The totality of the evidence was sufficient to allow the court to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant, who was the director of a private organization which maintained a nonprofit facility to house rescued dogs, did not provide proper care to multiple dogs because he exposed those dogs to conditions injurious to their well-being by confining them during cold weather in small cages, without bedding, in a facility that, in view of the nature of the confinement, provided inadequate heat for the size and breed of the dogs, when the dogs were exhibiting signs of imminent hypothermia; [2]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-247(a) was not void for vagueness, as applied to the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

404 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


AC 36476


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


160 Conn. App. 251; 124 A.3d 966; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 350


May 26, 2015, Argued 
October 6, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Davis, 320 Conn. 901, 127 A.3d 185, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 407 (Conn., Nov. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while having an elevated blood alcohol content, bribery of a witness, threatening in the second degree, breach of the peace in the second degree and interfering with an officer, and, in the second part, with being a persistent offender and with having previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Fuger, J.; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to the charge of threatening in the second degree and denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to the charge of bribery of a witness; verdict of guilty of operating a motor vehicle while having an elevated blood alcohol content, bribery of a witness, breach of the peace in the second degree and interfering with an officer; subsequently, the defendant was tried to the court on the second part of the information; judgment of guilty of having [***2] previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: OLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of bribery of a witness (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-149(a)), as it established that he told an officer that he offered money to a man whose vehicle he had hit in order to avoid police involvement and that he had consumed almost a liter of liquor prior to the accident, and the existence of an official proceeding at the time of the offer was not an element of the offense; [2]-Section 53a-149(a) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, as he had reasonably adequate notice that, after driving under the influence of alcohol, his efforts to alter the conduct of a likely adverse witness would constitute bribery of a witness; [3]-He was properly convicted of being a third time DUI offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g)(3) because the state sufficiently proved his two prior DUI convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

405 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parnoff


AC 36567


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


160 Conn. App. 270; 125 A.3d 573; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 349


May 19, 2015, Argued 
October 6, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Parnoff, 320 Conn. 901, 127 A.3d 185, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 406 (Conn., Nov. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of criminal mischief in the fourth degree, disorderly conduct and larceny in the sixth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two; thereafter, the trial court, Dennis, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of larceny in the sixth degree; subsequently, the remaining charges were tried to the jury before Dennis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of disorderly conduct, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's (D) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a)(1) conviction was not supported by sufficient evidence as his statement to a water company employee that he would get a gun and shoot him and another employee if they did not leave his property did not constitute fighting words under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I; [2]-D did not engage in violent, tumultuous or threatening behavior as the average person would not have reacted with imminent violence; [2]-D was shirtless and did not appear to have a gun; [3]-D warned the employees that he would leave, retrieve a gun, and shoot them if they did not leave, but he did not go into his home; [4]-The conditional nature of the statement reduced the probability of a imminent violence; [5]-D had been informed that two unknown individuals were on his property and did not commit any actions consistent with his statement.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Case remanded with direction.

 

406 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Braham v. Newbould


AC 36235


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


160 Conn. App. 294; 124 A.3d 977; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 347


May 27, 2015, Argued 
October 6, 2015, Officially Released.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged violation of the plaintiff's federal constitutional rights, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Zemetis, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court, A. Robinson, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for reargument, and adopted the previous ruling granting the motion to dismiss, and the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Braham v. Newbould, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2005 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 3, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiff inmate sued defendants, employees of a prison heath center, in connection with a $ 3 fee he was charged for obtaining eyeglasses, the trial court properly dismissed his § 1983 claim for money damages against defendants in their individual capacities; they were entitled to qualified immunity because plaintiff did not allege a deprivation of medical care sufficiently serious to constitute a violation of the Eighth Amendment; [2]-His § 1983 claim against defendants in their official capacities for declaratory and injunctive relief was properly dismissed; as he had received the eyeglasses, there was no prospective injunctive relief available to him on his Eighth Amendment claim; [3]-His state laws claims were barred by sovereign immunity, as he did not sufficiently allege constitutional violations and conduct in excess of defendants' statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

407 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Turn of River Fire Dep't, Inc. v. City of Stamford


AC 36468, AC 36465


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


159 Conn. App. 708; 123 A.3d 909; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 323


March 9, 2015, Argued 
September 15, 2015, Officially Released.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions, in two cases, for, inter alia, declaratory and injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the matters were consolidated and tried to the court, Hon. David R. Tobin, judge trial referee; judgment for the defendants in the first case and judgment in part for the plaintiffs in the second case, from which the plaintiffs in the first case and the plaintiffs in the second case appealed to this court; thereafter, the named plaintiff et al. in the first case and the plaintiffs in the second case withdrew their appeals.
Turn of River Fire Dep'T v. City of Stamford, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2900 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 13, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Stamford, Conn., Charter § C5-40-3(a) and (f) did not require a fire company to forfeit its existence as a private corporation because the charter amendments were most reasonably construed as applying only to those volunteer fire companies that voluntarily elected to provide fire protection to the city; [2]-Consequently, only if the fire company chose to continue to serve the city in the capacity of a fire company would it be subject to the provisions of § C5-40-3, as amended; [3]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-301 did not prohibit the fire department from superseding the volunteer fire companies because that statute pertained only to fire departments established by ordinance; [4]-Because the fire company maintained significant, even if not complete and unfettered, autonomy to continue using its private property to continue providing fire protection services to the city, the charter amendments did not unconstitutionally take that property in violation of the Fifth Amendment.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

 

408 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Angel R.


AC 36692


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


157 Conn. App. 826; 118 A.3d 117; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 218


November 20, 2014, Argued 
June 16, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Angel R., 317 Conn. 923, 118 A.3d 549, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 227 (Conn., July 22, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the respondent minor a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Juvenile Matters at Bridgeport, where the respondent was presented to the court, B. Kaplan, J., on a plea of guilty to assault of a public safety officer; judgment adjudicating the respondent minor delinquent and committing the respondent minor to the custody of the Commissioner of Children and Families; thereafter, the court denied the respondent minor's motion to dismiss and granted the motion filed by the petitioner, the Commissioner of Children and Families, to transfer custody of the respondent minor to the Department of Correction, and the respondent minor appealed to this court.
In re Angel R., 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 868 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 8, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-12(a) was not void for vagueness as applied to a juvenile because the record amply supported the conclusion that she had exhibited physically dangerous behavior while in custody and had been adjudicated delinquent on the basis of a physical assault, and a person of ordinary intelligence in the respondent's circumstances would comprehend that the assaultive behavior exhibited could be found to present a danger to others; [2]-The court held that the juvenile was not entitled to a jury trial at the transfer hearing as a child's best interests and the community's concerns are adequately protected by a hearing before a judge under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-12(a) and the statute contemplates a continuing role in monitoring a juvenile's well-being who is in custody.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

 

409 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ogden v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Columbia


AC 36516


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


157 Conn. App. 656; 117 A.3d 986; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 213


February 17, 2015, Argued 
June 2, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Ogden v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 321 (Conn., Oct. 7, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the defendant upholding an order issued to the plaintiff by the zoning enforcement officer of the Town of Columbia to cease and desist certain activities on certain of the plaintiff's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Hon. Lawrence C. Klaczak, judge trial referee; judgment sustaining the appeal; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to reargue, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Ogden v. Columbia Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1576 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 16, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In sustaining plaintiff's appeal from a zoning board of appeals' decision upholding an order requiring him to cease and desist from using his property as a construction/contractor's yard (CCY), the trial court erred in finding the CCY regulations unconstitutionally vague as applied to plaintiff; he failed to meet his burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he lacked adequate notice that the regulations applied to him, as the cease and desist orders made him aware of this, and he did not show that he was the victim of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement; [2]-The evidence supported the board's finding because it established that plaintiff used his property to house construction equipment and met with his employees there before traveling to construction sites with them, and that ads for his construction business listed his property as the business's address.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

410 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tilus


AC 35567


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


157 Conn. App. 453; 117 A.3d 920; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 195


January 5, 2015, Argued 
May 26, 2015, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Tilus, 317 Conn. 915, 117 A.3d 854, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 224 (July 8, 2015)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Dismissed without prejudice by, in part Tilus v. Warden, State Prison, 2016 Conn. Super. LEXIS 72 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 11, 2016)
Appeal dismissed by State v. Tilus, 323 Conn. 784, 151 A.3d 382, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 378 (Dec. 27, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Kavanewsky, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Louis, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2953 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 26, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment right to conflict-free counsel as it adequately canvassed him about his wish to proceed with retained counsel who also represented codefendant by informing him of the risks attendant to counsel's representation of him, and he stated he was aware of counsel's obligations to codefendant and expressed his desire to proceed with his counsel; [2]-The court did not violate defendant's right to present a defense by inducing codefendant to invoke his privilege against self-incrimination, but properly advised him of his constitutional rights without exercising undue influence on him; [3]-The prosecutor's reference to a defense witness as "muscle" defendant recruited to be an enforcer in the robbery was improper as it misstated the evidence, but defendant was not deprived of a fair trial as the case against him was strong.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

411 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


AC 32803


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


156 Conn. App. 537; 113 A.3d 103; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 134


October 16, 2014, Argued 
April 14, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 26, 2015.
Appeal denied by State v. Smith, 317 Conn. 910, 115 A.3d 1106, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 199 (Conn., June 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Fuger, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere to the second part of the information; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict and for a new trial; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and plea, and sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Admission of cell phone tracking information, if erroneous, was harmless because defendant's truck was involved in the robbery, defendant was the principal driver on the morning of the robbery, defendant matched the physical descriptions of the first robber, and defendant's DNA was recovered from a crack in the windshield of the truck; [2]-The court did not err by admitting a written statement into evidence under Conn. Code Evid. R. § 8-5 because detectives testified that the witness calmed down upon learning that they were investigating defendant's truck, and he testified that he was happy to provide the detectives with a DNA sample because it would exclude him as a suspect; [3]-The court did not improperly question a witness because the inquiry did not pertain to the merits of the case or the substance of the statement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

412 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lafleur


AC 35418


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


156 Conn. App. 289; 113 A.3d 472; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 123


January 14, 2015, Argued 
April 7, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lafleur, 317 Conn. 906, 114 A.3d 1221, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 179 (Conn., May 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with one count of the crime of assault in the third degree and three counts of the crime of violating a protective order, and substitute two part information, in the second case, charging the defendant in the first part with one count of the crime of assault in the first degree and one count of violation of the conditions of release in the first degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Holden, J., granted the state's motion to consolidate the cases; thereafter, the cases were tried to a jury; verdict of guilty, in the first case, of one count of assault in the third degree and two counts of violating a protective order, and, in the second case, of all counts; subsequently, the defendant pleaded guilty to being a persistent dangerous felony offender and the court rendered judgments of guilty in accordance with the verdicts and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to the Supreme Court, which affirmed the judgment in the first case, reversed the judgment in the second case, vacated the defendant's [***2] sentence, and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of acquittal in the second case and to resentence the defendant accordingly; on remand, the court, Holden, J., rendered a judgment of acquittal in the second case and imposed a new sentence in the first case, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. LaFleur, 307 Conn. 115, 51 A.3d 1048, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 352 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not improperly rely on the aggregate package theory of resentencing because it correctly followed the supreme court's remand order; [2]-It did not violate defendant's right to due process because defendant failed to demonstrate that a presumption of vindictiveness existed by virtue of a greater sentence imposed at the resentencing proceeding; [3]-The correct approach was to compare, in the aggregate, the sentence imposed following a successful appeal with that which was imposed prior to the appeal to determine if the second sentence constitutes a greater penalty; [4]-Defendant's second sentence was not more severe than his aggregate original sentence; [5]-The trial court did not violate defendant's right against double jeopardy because his sentence following remand was the result of his successful appeal, and the trial court properly resentenced him.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Davis


AC 35605


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


156 Conn. App. 175; 111 A.3d 567; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 118


October 23, 2014, Argued 
March 31, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Davis, 317 Conn. 921, 118 A.3d 62, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 221 (2015)
Appeal denied by State v. Davis, 317 Conn. 920, 117 A.3d 856, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 236 (2015)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Davis, 2017 Conn. LEXIS 69 (Conn., Mar. 14, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of criminal possession of a firearm, carrying a pistol without a permit, altering firearm identification marks, unlawful possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, attempt to assault a police officer, reckless endangerment in the first degree, interfering with an officer, and with the infraction of reckless driving, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and counts two through eight were tried to the jury before B. Fischer, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of carrying a pistol without a permit, unlawful possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, reckless endangerment in the first degree, interfering with an officer and reckless driving; thereafter, the first count was tried to the court, B. Fischer, J.; judgment of guilty of criminal possession of a firearm, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Davis, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2787 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 24, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was insufficient to sustain defendant's convictions for carrying a pistol without a permit and unlawful possession of a weapon in a vehicle under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 29-35 and 29-38 because there was no direct evidence of his residence or place of business, his conduct, even if indicative of consciousness of guilt, could not, without impermissible speculation, relieve the State of its burden of proving he lacked a valid permit, and it was possible that he possessed a valid permit from the local authority of his residence or place of business under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-28(b); [2]-There was no violation of defendant's due process rights because he did not object to the trial court's alleged improprieties at trial and the court was free to intervene to clarify testimony and assist the jury in understanding the evidence so long as it was nonpartisan in doing so.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and judgment directed.

 

414 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gorski v. McIsaac


AC 36446


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


156 Conn. App. 195; 112 A.3d 201; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 119


December 9, 2014, Argued 
March 31, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the defendant for modification of an award of child support issued in connection with a foreign judgment of dissolution, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Albis, J., denied the motion, and the defendant appealed to this court.
Gorski v. McIsaac, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 17 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 7, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an appeal involving modification of child support, as to the daughter's domicile, although she might reside for a time in her dormitory at school or, from time to time, at defendant father's home, her true, fixed and permanent home at the time of the hearing was plaintiff mother's home; [2]-As to the daughter's principal dependence, although the father contributed to the daughter's education and support, he was not the primary source of that support; [3]-The mother was the primary source of the daughter's support and thus, the daughter was principally dependent on the mother for her maintenance; [4]-The father failed to demonstrate that Mass. Gen. Laws ch. 208, § 28, was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case because the statutory terms "domiciled" and "principally dependent" were not ambiguous where those terms had usual and accepted meanings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

415 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Houghtaling


AC 35720


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


155 Conn. App. 794; 111 A.3d 931; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 89


November 21, 2014, Argued 
March 17, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Houghtaling, 317 Conn. 919, 118 A.3d 62, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 223 (July 15, 2015)
affirmed on other grounds by State v. Houghtaling, 2017 Conn. LEXIS 225 (Conn., July 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of more than four ounces of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, where the court, Riley, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court affirmed defendant's drug possession convictions because the trial court properly determined that he lacked standing to challenge the search of the property as the evidence and testimony failed to demonstrate that his relationship with the property was personal in nature or that it was more than sporadic, irregular or inconsequential, as he did not establish that he was a cotenant, the fact that there was some mail in the kitchen with his name on it did not support his contention that he was at the property frequently, and his claims that he made home improvements and that he slept there were unsupported by the facts in the record; [2]-Thus, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained from the search of the property because he did not have a subjective expectation of privacy in the property at the time of the search.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

416 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nowacki


AC 34577


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


155 Conn. App. 758; 111 A.3d 911; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 77


October 22, 2014, Argued 
March 10, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Three informations charging the defendant, in the first case, with the crime of disorderly conduct and with the infraction of operating a motor vehicle with intent to harass or intimidate, in the second case, with the crime of harassment in the second degree, and, in the third case, with criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the court, Hudock, J., granted the state's motion for joinder; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of harassment in the second degree and criminal violation of a protective order, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Nowacki, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 720 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 19, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where a pro se defendant was convicted of criminal violation of a protective order based on his sending an email to the alleged victim, which he testified he did by mistake, the trial court reversibly erred in denying him a subpoena for a witness whom he claimed was the intended recipient and in refusing to permit him to explain his relationship with the witness, as this violated his right to compulsory process and to present a meaningful defense; [2]-His second-degree harassment conviction violated his First Amendment right to free speech; Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2) was unconstitutional as applied to him because his conviction was dependent on the content of his email to the alleged victim, rather than the manner in which it was communicated, and his threat to take legal action against her was not a "true threat" that fell outside the realm of protected speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

417 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Verrillo v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Branford


AC 36196


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


155 Conn. App. 657; 111 A.3d 473; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 80


November 19, 2014, Argued 
March 10, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision by the named defendant granting the application for variances filed by the defendant Linda F. Lantsberger et al., brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Blue, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendants, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Verrillo v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Branford, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 642 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 22, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in sustaining plaintiff's appeal of a zoning board of appeals' grant of variances. HOLDINGS: [1]-The applicants' inability under the regulations to renovate and expand their legally existing nonconforming residence was personal in nature and not a proper basis for a finding of hardship that justified granting the variances; [2]-As the applicants were not completely or almost completely deprived of the use of the value of their land, a denial of the requested variance would not amount to a "practical confiscation" or be "tantamount to confiscation"; [3]-As the proposed use would increase the nonconformity, it was not "far less offensive'" than the existing use; thus, the Adolphson exception to the hardship requirement did not apply; [4]-The applicants did not show that the proposed use would not substantially affect the comprehensive zoning plan.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

418 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Book


AC 35947


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


155 Conn. App. 560; 109 A.3d 1027; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 66


October 23, 2014, Argued 
March 3, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Book, 318 Conn. 901, 122 A.3d 632, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 277 (2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Book v. Connecticut, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3269 (U.S., May 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of harassment in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Povodator, J., dismissed one count of harassment in the second degree; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Book v. Tobin, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 17275 (D. Conn., Aug. 16, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a), proscribing harassment, was not unconstitutional because it could be constitutionally applied to speech if the content of that speech rose to the level of a true threat, which was unprotected by the first amendment; [2]-Sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction for harassment because defendant's letter was likely to cause alarm or annoyance to the victim, who had been the complainant in defendant's previous harassment case, knowing that she did not want to hear from him. The jury could reasonably have found that defendant sent the letter with the intent to harass or alarm the victim and his belief regarding the validity of the 2001 conviction and the fact that there was no prohibition in place at the time were not dispositive on the issue of whether the communication was sent with the intent to harass, alarm, or annoy the victim.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Bullock


AC 35006


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


155 Conn. App. 1; 107 A.3d 503; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 13


September 16, 2014, Argued 
January 20, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bullock, 316 Conn. 906, 111 A.3d 882, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 112 (Conn., Mar. 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, attempt to commit assault in the first degree, carrying a pistol without a permit and reckless endangerment in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Kavanewsky, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a mistrial; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, carrying a pistol without a permit and reckless endangerment in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Bullock, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1885 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 27, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court did not err by declining a jury instruction pertaining to the fallibility of eyewitness identification evidence because defendant was taken into police custody at the crime scene just moments after the shooting; it was what police observed, defendant's clothing, and his physical presence at the time of the shooting, that led to his arrest; [2]-The court properly admitted evidence related to a prior shooting under Conn. Code Evid. R. 4-5 because it was not presented to demonstrate that defendant had engaged in any type of crime, wrong, or act in connection with the prior shooting; [3]-Defendant's request to charge did not adequately preserve the issue for review under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 42-16 because the isolated statement could not have alerted the court that the argument was meant to apply to attempt to commit assault.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. McNeil


AC 34491


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


154 Conn. App. 727; 106 A.3d 320; 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 5

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. McNeil, 316 Conn. 908, 111 A.3d 884, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 110 (Conn., Apr. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the infraction of operating an unregistered motor vehicle, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics, possession with intent to use drug paraphernalia and larceny in the sixth degree, and with the infraction of operating a motor vehicle without minimum insurance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district Hartford, geographical area number twelve, where the information in the second case was tried to the jury before C. Johnson v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 35368


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


153 Conn. App. 848; 104 A.3d 771; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 497


September 24, 2014, Argued 
December 2, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Johnson v. Comm'r of Corr., 315 Conn. 912, 106 A.3d 305, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 25 (Conn., Jan. 6, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Newson, J.; thereafter, the petition was withdrawn in part; judgment denying the petition; subsequently, the court granted the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
Johnson v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 51 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 7, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The habeas court did not err in denying a petition for a writ of habeas corpus because the use of the wrong docket number on some documents constituted a circumstantial defect under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-123; [2]-The State both intended to and consistently did reference the proper party in prosecuting petitioner for the victim's death; [3]-Petitioner was plainly informed as to which of the two files on which the State was proceeding to trial because both informations charged him with the same offense based on the same facts; [4]-Because any reference to the incorrect docket during and after petitioner's trial qualified as a circumstantial defect under § 52-123, any attempt to challenge his prosecution and conviction on that ground would have inevitably failed; [5]-Thus, petitioner's counsel were not ineffective for failing to raise that issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Gen. Stat. § 6-38a(a).

Town of Bethlehem v. Acker


35463


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

February 11, 2014, Argued 
October 14, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Town of Bethlehem v. Acker, 315 Conn. 908, 105 A.3d 235, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 495 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Verified petition seeking, inter alia, custody in favor of the named plaintiff of certain animals in the defendants' possession that allegedly were neglected, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Trombley, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiffs, from which the named defendant appealed and the named plaintiff cross appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, Trombley, J., issued an articulation of its decision.

DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a nonprofit dog rescue facility was properly found to have neglected dogs, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a, when the dogs were kept in a barn with an average temperature of 30 degrees Fahrenheit. HOLDINGS: [1]-The court applied the correct legal standards and properly determined that the smaller breed dogs were neglected and that the larger breed dogs were not neglected; [2]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts of the case; [3]-The court did not err in declining to admit the rebuttal testimony offered by the facility; [4]-The court did not err in granting the town's request for injunctive relief and properly transferred ownership of the smaller breed dogs to the town; [5]-The court's order directing the parties to agree among themselves which of the dogs removed from the facility were smaller breed dogs was vague.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part. Case remanded for further proceedings.

Marasco v. Conn. Reg'l Vocational-Technical Sch. Sys.


AC 35169


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


153 Conn. App. 146; 100 A.3d 930; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 407


April 21, 2014, Argued 
September 30, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Marasco v. Conn. Reg'l Vocational-Technical Sch. Sys., 2015 Conn. LEXIS 86 (Conn., Mar. 11, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged age discrimination, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Dooley, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Marasco v. Conn. Reg'l Vocational-Technical Sch. Sys., 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2572 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 4, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Improper form of judgment; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a trial court properly granted summary judgment to a school system on a teacher's claim that the school system had discriminated against him in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60, or in violation of the federal Age Discrimination in Employment Act of 1967 (ADEA), 29 U.S.C.S. § 621 et seq., and on his claim of retaliation. HOLDINGS: [1]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100 explicitly waived the State of Connecticut's sovereign immunity for claims against the State for employment discrimination brought under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60; [2]-The school system was immune from suit whether in state or federal court, on the basis of an alleged violation of the ADEA; [3]-The trial court properly rendered summary judgment in favor of the school system because the teacher's claims amounted to bare conclusory assertions that the school system had discriminated and retaliated against him.


OUTCOME: Improper form of judgment, and judgment directed in part.

HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly granted the second petition to extend defendant's commitment; [2]-Not only did defendant fail to clearly articulate his claim that the order continuing his commitment violated his equal protection rights during his argument, he also did not litigate it. State v. Abraham


AC 35706


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


152 Conn. App. 709; 99 A.3d 1258; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 385


May 27, 2014, Argued 
September 9, 2014, Officially Released.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Licari, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm and of criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, and sentence enhanced for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court; thereafter, the Supreme Court denied the defendant's petition for certification to appeal; subsequently, the court, Fasano, J., dismissed the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Abraham, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2719 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The motion court erred in dismissing, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence. The motion court had jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 43-22 to consider the whether the sentencing court erred by enhancing defendant's sentence under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-202k without first obtaining the necessary jury finding; [2]-The matter had to be remanded to motion court because the record was inadequate to determine if defendant did not personally waive his right under § 53-202k to a jury determination of whether, in committing the underlying felony, he used, displayed, or represented that he possessed a firearm, thereby resulting in a sentence imposed in an illegal manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Chief Disciplinary Counsel v. Zelotes


AC 35867


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


152 Conn. App. 380; 98 A.3d 852; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 364


April 22, 2014, Argued 
August 19, 2014, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Chief Disciplinary Counsel v. Zelotes, 314 Conn. 944, 102 A.3d 1116, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 438 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment by the plaintiff for alleged professional misconduct by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the court, Hon. Frank H. D'Andrea, Jr., judge trial referee; judgment suspending the defendant from the practice of law for five months, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Disciplinary Counsel v. Zelotes, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1451 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 28, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that the trial court's finding that a lawyer violated Conn. R. R. Prof. Conduct 8.4(a) as well because the record showed that his behavior created a significant risk that his representation of the client would be materially affected by his personal interest, and, thus, the timing and totality of his behavior, rather than the time, place and manner of his dating, was prejudicial to the administration of justice; [3]-The attorney was suspended from the practice of law for five years for his misconduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Avoletta v. State


AC 35704


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


152 Conn. App. 177; 98 A.3d 839; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 358


April 24, 2014, Argued 
August 12, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Avoletta v. State, 314 Conn. 944, 102 A.3d 1116, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 431 (Conn., Nov. 12, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged violation of the plaintiffs' rights to a free appropriate public education for children in a safe school setting, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Sheridan, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Avoletta v. State, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1049 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 6, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in dismissing a suit against the State filed by plaintiffs, children and their mother, alleging it violated their constitutional rights to a free appropriate public education in a safe school setting. HOLDINGS: [1]-The court properly found that the action was untimely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a), as plaintiffs discovered a harm by the time the children were taken out of the public schools but did not file a claim with the Claims Commissioner until over a year later; [2]-The court properly found that the legislature's resolution, which vacated the Commissioner's decision that plaintiffs' claim was untimely and allowed them to sue the State, was proscribed by Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 as a public emolument, because the resolution did not serve a public purpose but merely provided plaintiffs with an exclusive and private benefit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dickerson


AC 35725


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


151 Conn. App. 658; 97 A.3d 15; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 333


May 21, 2014, Argued 
July 22, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Dickerson, 314 Conn. 926, 101 A.3d 271, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 381 (Conn., Oct. 15, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree, and with the crime of sexual assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the defendant was presented to the court, Lager, J., on a plea of guilty; judgment of guilty; thereafter, the court, Holden, J., denied the defendant's motion for an exemption from sex offender registration, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Lifetime registration requirement of Megan's Law, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 54-250 to 54-261, imposed on defendant under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-252 for his conviction of a violent sexual assault--engaging in sexual intercourse with a mentally defective victim--did not violate his right to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Though he was similarly situated to persons convicted of nonviolent second degree sexual assaults, who were subject to a 10-year registration period, the classification was rationally related to the State's legitimate interest in protecting the public from sex offenders whose actions demonstrated a willingness to use force or the threat of force to overcome the will of victims who had not consented to intercourse; [2]-His equal protection challenge under Conn. Const. art. I, § 20 failed as it was not materially different from his federal challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Henderson v. State


AC 34944


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


151 Conn. App. 246; 95 A.3d 1; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 299


January 8, 2014, Argued 
July 1, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Blue, J., granted the named plaintiff's motion to cite in Jess Daenekindt as a party plaintiff; subsequently, the court, A. Robinson, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the named defendant et al. and rendered judgment thereon, from which the named plaintiff appealed to this court; thereafter, the action was withdrawn as against the defendant city of Meriden et al.
State v. Henderson, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2050 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 29, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a business owner's action against the State of Connecticut and a senior assistant state's attorney for breach of contract was properly dismissed. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly granted the State of Connecticut's and the attorney's motion to dismiss on the ground of sovereign immunity because the owner alleged claims against the attorney only in her official capacity, and the action against her was, in effect, against the State. Moreover, the owner failed to plead sufficiently that the State, as represented by the attorney in her official capacity, acted in excess of statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

150 Conn. App. 472; 91 A.3d 932; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 235

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion in suspending defendant from the practice of law for two years because it found that the attorney demonstrated a pattern of misconduct, resulting in violations of Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 1.2(a), 1.3, 1.4, 1.7(a)(2), 4.4(a), and 8.4, and that, at the time he committed the violations, he was a seasoned member of the bar; [2]-The attorney had previously been disciplined for professional misconduct, and the trial court found that he committed acts of misconduct that violated his duty to the public, the legal system and the profession; [3]-The trial court did not err in refusing to reconsider the attorney's preclusion claims because the attorney made no offer of proof as to any new information that he intended to introduce in support of those claims that was not already before the trial court.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

AC 35143


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


150 Conn. App. 576; 92 A.3d 961; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 232


December 9, 2013, Argued 
May 27, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by We the People of Conn., Inc. v. Malloy, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 353 (Conn., Oct. 8, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of certain executive orders issued by the defendant, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Graham, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A declaratory judgment action to determine the validity of certain executive orders issued by the Governor was moot because legislation that passed, establishing collective bargaining for family child care providers and personal care attendants, 2012 Conn. Stat. § 17b-705 et seq.), entirely replaced the executive orders and, thus, even if the executive orders were rescinded, the legislation would still be in place; the claims by the two groups at issue did not fall under the "capable of repetition yet evading review" exception to the mootness doctrine.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Morneau v. State


AC 35423


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


150 Conn. App. 237; 90 A.3d 1003; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 214


October 22, 2013, Argued 
May 20, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Morneau v. State, 312 Conn. 926, 95 A.3d 522, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 274 (Conn., July 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged violations of federal law, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Domnarski, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the named defendant et al. and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Morneau v. State, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3106 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 21, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court properly determined that the resolution passed by the Connecticut General Assembly granting plaintiff permission to bring suit against the marshals and the State Marshal Commission constituted an exclusive public emolument in violation of Conn. Const. art. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

437 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edwards


AC 34279


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


148 Conn. App. 760; 87 A.3d 1144; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 100


November 15, 2013, Argued 
March 18, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Keegan, J., judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in finding that defendant violated his probation because he was arrested for failing to provide notification of an address change under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-251(a) as homelessness did not always equal a change of address; [2]-Although defendant could have been living in a warehouse, or his truck on the premises of his former home and could have been considered homeless because he had been evicted and was without a dwelling in either instance, he would have experienced a change of address only if he was found to have been living in the warehouse; [3]-Living in the truck on the premises of his former home was not a change of residence address because defendant's location remained the same; [4]-Section 54-251(a) did not suggest that a registrant needed to specify where on a particular piece of property he was actually residing.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Case remanded with direction.

State v. Smith

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


148 Conn. App. 684; 86 A.3d 498; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 95

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit robbery in the first degree and attempt to commit kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Prescott, J.; verdict of guilty of attempt to commit robbery in the first degree; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant attempted to have the complainant return money he had sent to her for a bail bond or a lawyer, the evidence was insufficient to convict him of attempt to commit first degree robbery (Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a)(2) and 53a-134(a)(3)). Because defendant owned the property he sought to retake, the evidence was insufficient to establish his intent to commit larceny; therefore, the State did not prove the intent element of the crime of attempt to commit first-degree robbery.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Traylor v. Gerratana

148 Conn. App. 605; 88 A.3d 552; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 93

State v. Hector M.


AC 34642


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


148 Conn. App. 378; 85 A.3d 1188; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 65


November 20, 2013, Argued 
February 25, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hector M., 311 Conn. 936, 88 A.3d 550, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 115 (Conn., Apr. 2, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with eight counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, seven counts of the crime of sexual assault in the second degree and seven counts of the crime of sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Cremins, J.; judgment of guilty of three counts of risk of injury to a child, and two counts each of sexual assault in the second degree and sexual assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of second- and third-degree sexual assault (Conn. Gen. In re Shane M.


AC 35819


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


148 Conn. App. 308; 84 A.3d 1265; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 57


November 14, 2013, Argued 
February 3, 2014, Officially Released*


* February 3, 2014, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by In re Shane M., 311 Conn. 930, 86 A.3d 1056, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 94 (2014)
Affirmed by In re Shane M., 2015 Conn. LEXIS 249 (Conn., Aug. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition by the Commissioner of Children and Families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters at Hartford, and tried to the court, Burgdorff, J.; judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent father appealed to this court.
In re Shane M., 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1027 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 30, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:

Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) was not limited to conduct contemplated by the specific steps; [2]-The evidence supported the finding that the father did not achieve a sufficient degree of personal rehabilitation because he failed to adequately address his substance abuse, mental health, and domestic violence issues; [3]-The father's claim that § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) was unconstitutionally vague as applied lacked merit because he was provided with sufficient notification, he had a reasonable opportunity to comply with the specific steps, and a reasonably intelligent person would have known that his conduct would be a basis to terminate his parental rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Chance


AC 34393


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


147 Conn. App. 598; 83 A.3d 703; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 12


September 12, 2013, Argued 
January 21, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Chance, 311 Conn. 932, 87 A.3d 580, 2014 Conn. LEXIS 91 (2014)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Chance v. Conn., 2014 U.S. LEXIS 6202 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the jury before Marano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child, kidnapping in the second degree, attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, and unlawful restraint in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Chance v. Chance, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1191 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 7, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed. affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-There was sufficient evidence to support the defendant's conviction of kidnapping in the second degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94 because his actions of asking the victim to get in his truck, chasing her when she refused his invitations, pulling her ponytail and forcing her to the ground, putting his hand over her mouth to suppress her screams, and attempting to pick her up were consistent with the elements of the charged crimes. On the basis of the victim's testimony, the jury reasonably could have found that the defendant possessed the requisite intent to prevent her liberation; [2]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94(a) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant because his restraint of the victim was coupled with strong evidence of his intent to prevent the victim's liberation. Thus, § 53a-94(a) afforded him adequate notice that his behavior was prohibited.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions to vacate the conviction for attempt to commit kidnapping.

Garcia v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 33827


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


147 Conn. App. 669; 84 A.3d 1; 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 11


October 23, 2013, Argued 
January 21, 2014, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Garcia v. Comm'r of Corr., 2014 Conn. LEXIS 201 (Conn., May 29, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Schuman, J., granted the respondent's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Garcia v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1746 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 8, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A decision of the United States Supreme Court, which held that police could search a vehicle incident to a recent occupant's arrest only if the arrestee was within reaching distance of the passenger compartment at the time of the search, or it was reasonable to believe the vehicle contained evidence of the offense of arrest, did not apply retroactively; [2]-The rule applied to the conduct of police when executing a search; [3]-Therefore, it was not substantive because it did not narrow the conduct or class of persons punishable pursuant to a criminal statute; [4]-The accuracy of any trial was not necessarily determined by the fact that evidence was seized in violation of the rule; [5]-Evidence obtained from a search that violates the Fourth Amendment does not automatically result in an inaccurate verdict which requires a new trial.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment affirmed.

Hadden, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, matter was tried to the jury; subsequently, the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to one count of interfering with an officer and denied the defendant's motion for a mistrial; verdict of guilty of increasing speed in an attempt to escape or elude an officer and interfering with an officer; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

State v. Dickman


AC 33781


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


146 Conn. App. 17; 75 A.3d 780; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 466


April 22, 2013, Argued 
September 24, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Dickman, 310 Conn. 948, 80 A.3d 905, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 435 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the jury before Carbonneau, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a mistrial; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Dickman v. Office of State Ethics, 140 Conn. App. 754, 60 A.3d 297, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 101 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of second-degree forgery (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-139(a), as jury reasonably could have found that doctors' notes she altered, as part of scheme concerning benefits related to leaves of absence and returns to work, did or could "affect a legal right or interest" within the meaning of § 53a-139(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of four counts of second-degree forgery (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-139(a)), as the jury reasonably could have found that the doctors' notes she altered, as part of scheme concerning benefits related to leaves of absence and returns to work, did or could "affect a legal right or interest" within the meaning of § 53a-139(a)(1); [2]-The doctors' notes, a fitness for duty form, a medical certificate, a certificate for return to work, and worker status reports were properly admitted; as none of them were used to prove the truth of the matter asserted therein, they were not hearsay; [3]-As defendant did not meet her burden to show prejudice resulting from the prosecution's late disclosure, or her attorney's late discovery, of allegedly exculpatory evidence, the trial court did not err in denying her motion for a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gonzalez v. State Elections Enforcement Comm'n

State v. Braswell


AC 33053


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


145 Conn. App. 617; 76 A.3d 231; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 442


June 3, 2013, Argued 
September 10, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Braswell, 310 Conn. 939, 79 A.3d 892, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 423 (2013)
Affirmed by State v. Braswell, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 256 (Conn., Sept. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Wenzel, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions to discharge counsel and to represent himself; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, Wenzel, J., issued an articulation of its decision.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in denying defendant's pretrial motion to dismiss his counsel and to represent himself, because he unequivocally asserted his right to self-representation, the court failed to determine if his waiver of counsel was knowing and intelligent, and improperly denied the motion based on his relationship with counsel and the state of discovery--factors that were irrelevant to his right to self-representation; [2]-The trial court properly denied his motion to suppress evidence seized from his "home," as he did not show he had a reasonable expectation of privacy with regard to the area that was searched; [3]-The warrantless seizure of DNA evidence from defendant's finger was justified by exigent circumstances; [4]-The trial court properly denied his motion to suppress his statements to police, as he did not show he was in custody or was being interrogated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Holloway v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 34511


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


145 Conn. App. 353; 77 A.3d 777; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 439


May 22, 2013, Argued 
September 3, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Newson, J.; judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
Holloway v. Warden, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 386 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 3, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court's instructions on the charge of possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a public housing project under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b) were constitutionally deficient under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because they omitted all reference to or explanation of the intended-location-of-sale element of that offense; [2]-By failing to object or except to those deficient instructions, defense counsel was ineffective under the performance prong of Strickland; [3]-The prejudice prong of Strickland was satisfied because the parties' stipulation as to the location of petitioner's arrest did not constitute a confession of the omitted element, and the evidence was by no means clear and uncontested that petitioner was engaged or about to engage in a drug sale at the time of his arrest.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

State v. Dunstan


AC 33789


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


145 Conn. App. 384; 74 A.3d 559; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 436


May 30, 2013, Argued 
September 3, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Dunstan, 310 Conn. 958, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 474 (Conn., Dec. 11, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of assault of public safety personnel and interfering with an officer, and with the crime of breach of the peace in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Carbonneau, J., denied the defendant's application for accelerated rehabilitation; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Newson, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's trial for assault of a public safety officer in violation of Conn. Gen. OUTCOME: Judgment reversed as to the conviction of interfering with an officer; affirmed in all other respects.

Albini v. Conn. Med. Examining Bd.


AC 33462


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


144 Conn. App. 337; 72 A.3d 1208; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 360


January 11, 2013, Argued 
July 23, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, Cohn, J. Appeal from the decision of the defendant ordering the plaintiffs to cease and desist from practicing medicine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, and tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal; thereafter, the court granted in part the plaintiffs' motion to reconsider and to reargue and dismissed the appeal, and the plaintiffs appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.
Albini v. Conn. Med. Examining Bd., 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 860 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 5, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-179(a) did not require the midwives to present oral argument, thus, the trial court properly determined that the midwives were not barred from raising their claims on appeal and that it had jurisdiction over the case; [2]-The Connecticut Medical Examining Board (Board) exceeded its statutory authority by interpreting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-9 to include the diagnosis or assessment of conditions as the plain language of the statute defines the scope of the unauthorized practice of medicine; [3]-The Board exceeded the scope of its statutory authority by purportedly regulating midwifery as the unauthorized practice of medicine, as normal pregnancies are not considered illnesses, deformities, ailments or diseases, and, thus, a diagnosis or assessment rendered in relation to normal pregnancies would not place an individual's actions within the ambit of § 20-9.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, in part.

Dickman v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 34574


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


143 Conn. App. 780; 70 A.3d 1147; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 336


April 16, 2013, Argued 
July 2, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Hon. Joseph J. Purtill, judge trial referee; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Dickman v. Warden, State Prison, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 257 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 24, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A habeas corpus petitioner's challenge to the search of her work computer could not establish her claim of actual innocence as a matter of law because petitioner committed the acts that constituted the elements of the crime for which she was convicted, forger in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-140; [2]-Petitioner not only presented no evidence that she was factually innocent but actually admitted that she engaged in the conduct upon which her conviction was based; [3]-Because petitioner did not claim that she did not, in fact, commit the crime for which was convicted, her contention that the evidence upon which her conviction was based was obtained in violation of her constitutional rights was of no moment and thus, could not, as a matter of law, support a claim of actual innocence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
