State v. Banks


AC 33326, AC 33387


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


143 Conn. App. 485; 71 A.3d 582; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 328


February 15, 2013, Argued 
June 25, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at State v. Drakes, 143 Conn. App. 510, 70 A.3d 1104, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 324 (2013)
Appeal granted by State v. Banks, 310 Conn. 951, 81 A.3d 1179, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 461 (2013)
Affirmed by State v. Mark Banks, 2016 Conn. LEXIS 184 (Conn., June 1, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant in two consolidated cases with four counts each of the crimes of robbery in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, and with two counts of the crime of criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Spada, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty; thereafter, the court, Mullarkey, J., granted the state's motion for permission to use reasonable physical force to obtain a DNA sample and rendered judgment thereon; subsequently, the court, Mullarkey, J., granted the defendant's motion for a stay; thereafter, substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with refusing to submit to the taking of a blood or other biological sample for DNA analysis, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, and tried to the court, Carbonneau, J.; subsequently, the court, Carbonneau, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant filed separate appeals with this court; thereafter, this court consolidated the appeals.
State v. Banks, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 245 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 8, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]- The trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to grant the State's motion under former Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-102g (2003) to use reasonable force to take a DNA sample from defendant, a convicted felon, since a prosecution under § 54-102g for failing to provide a DNA sample applied prospectively to conduct that occurred after his sentence had begun; [2]-Application of § 54-102g to defendant based on crimes committed before its enactment did not violate his right to due process or the Ex Post Facto Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, as it was a regulatory statute, not a penal one, and it was not applied retroactively; [3]-Though former § 54-102g did not expressly permit the State to use reasonable force to obtain a DNA sample, the trial court properly found that not allowing the State to do so would fatally undermine the purpose of § 54-102g--to maintain a DNA data bank.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

AC 34291


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


141 Conn. App. 9; 60 A.3d 308; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 94


December 7, 2012, Argued 
February 19, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, a violation of the named plaintiff's state and federal constitutional rights during body cavity searches conducted in a state correctional facility, and for injunctive and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London where the court, Cosgrove, J., granted the defendant Michael R. Smith's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court denied the named plaintiff's motion for partial summary judgment and granted in part the cross motion for partial summary judgment filed by the named defendant et al., and the named plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Trial court's decision, granting, in part, defendants' cross motion for partial summary judgment, disposed of only part of plaintiff's complaint, namely, his claim for monetary damages, while his claims for injunctive relief remained pending before the trial court. Further, the trial court's decision did not dispose of all causes of actions against a particular party nor did the court make the requisite determinations to trigger the exceptions set forth in Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 61-3 and 61-4(a). As such, the trial court's decision was not an appealable final judgment.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.

C & H Mgmt., LLC v. City of Shelton


AC 33264


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


140 Conn. App. 608; 59 A.3d 851; 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 54


October 19, 2012, Argued 
February 5, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged taking by inverse condemnation of certain of the plaintiff's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the court, Doherty, J., denied the defendants' motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the court denied the defendants' motion to reargue and issued an articulation of its decision, and the defendants appealed to this court.
C&H Mgmt., LLC v. City of Shelton, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3367 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 23, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed; affirmed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A city and its engineer challenged an order denying their motion for summary judgment, which was grounded on the doctrine of res judicata. The city was the same party against whom a builder brought a prior mandamus action. However, the engineer, an individual, was not the same party against whom the mandamus action was brought, nor was he in privity with that municipal official. Accordingly, the builder's action against the engineer could not be barred by the doctrine of res judicata. The claims against the city were barred as they merged into the final judgment in the prior mandamus action.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and denied in part.

September 10, 2012, Argued 
November 20, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Fernandez v. Comm'r of Corr., 307 Conn. 947, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 23 (Conn., Jan. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Bright, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Fernandez v. Warden, State Prison, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 698 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 24, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: An inmate, who was serving a sentence on a conviction of drug-related offenses, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his assault conviction. The habeas court dismissed his petition for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, finding that he was not in custody. He appealed. The habeas court did in fact lack subject matter jurisdiction over his petition, because he had completed the sentence on the assault conviction on which the petition was based, and the fact that that conviction affected his parole eligibility did not render him in custody under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-466.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Parnoff v. Yuille


AC 32545


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


139 Conn. App. 147; 57 A.3d 349; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 532


May 24, 2012, Argued 
November 20, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Parnoff v. Yuille, 307 Conn. 956, 59 A.3d 1192, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 49 (2013)
On remand at, Motion granted by, Judgment entered by Parnoff v. Yuille, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1993 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hon. John P. Maiocco, Jr., judge trial referee, granted the motion to intervene as a defendant filed by Laura M. Mooney; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Tobin, J.; verdict in part for the plaintiff; subsequently, court denied the plaintiff's motion to reconsider and the named defendant's motion to set aside the verdict and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the plaintiff appealed and the named defendant cross appealed to this court.
Yuille v. Bridgeport Hosp., 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1336 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 11, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant former client appealed a judgment finding him contractually liable for attorney fees in an amount greater than allowed by the fee cap statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-251c. Where the fee agreement called for a contingency fee of 40 percent, the trial court effectively reformed the fee agreement to permit a recovery premised on a contract that violated public policy. Thus, the trial court should not have permitted the jury to consider the contract based claim and the jury's verdict on the contract counts could not stand.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Two part substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, and with operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension, and, in the second part, with having previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of conspiracy to commit false statement in the second degree, conspiracy to fabricate physical evidence, tampering with a witness and conspiracy to commit forgery in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, where the court, T. Gen. Stat. § 12-422 provided an adequate legal remedy, since it provided for legal relief and such relief as might be equitable, including interest, even though attorney's fees were not allowed.


OUTCOME: Judgment directed.

Estate of Bochicchio v. Quinn


AC 32895


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


136 Conn. App. 359; 46 A.3d 239; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 302


November 29, 2011, Argued 
June 26, 2012, Officially Released.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Bill of discovery seeking the defendants' deposition testimony concerning, inter alia, the security measures employed at the Middletown courthouse, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Domnarski, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Estate of Bochicchio v. Quinn, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2772 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 28, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider the merits of plaintiff's action. Plaintiff failed to exhaust its administrative remedies before the claims commission under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160. The commissioner had not made a final determination on the discovery process, nor the ultimate determination of whether plaintiff could sue the State. The discovery process before the commissioner remained an ongoing process. A premature ruling from a court could usurp the commissioner's legislative function and lead to an unnecessary conflict between the two branches of government.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Deshawn D.


AC 33504


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

June 26, 2012, Officially Released.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A trial court properly denied a motion of defendant, a juvenile, for a reduction in the term of his delinquency commitment because neither the plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d nor that of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-141d provided credit for predisposition detention when a juvenile offender was ordered committed to a period of confinement. Because defendant was committed to the custody of the department of children and families and not to the department of correction, § 18-98d was facially inapplicable to his detention circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Albright-Lazzari v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


AC 33444


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


136 Conn. App. 76; 44 A.3d 859; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 261


March 15, 2012, Argued 
June 5, 2012, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Albright-Lazzari v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 305 Conn. 927, 47 A.3d 886, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 322 (Conn., July 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the defendant determining that the department of children and families did not violate certain provisions of the Freedom of Information Act and dismissing the plaintiffs' complaint as to the department of children and families, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the department of children and families' motion to intervene as a defendant; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.
Albright-Lazzari v. Murphy, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1017 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 21, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Parents challenged a judgment dismissing their appeal from the decision of the Freedom of Information Commission. The Commission dismissed their action under the Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq., to obtain records from the Department of Children and Families on the ground that the records were exempt from disclosure under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-28. The Commission properly dismissed the complaint without a hearing because it did not have jurisdiction to determine rights of access under § 17a-28 to the Department's records on child protection activities.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Sullivan v. Lazzari


AC 32616


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


135 Conn. App. 831; 43 A.3d 750; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 256


February 8, 2012, Argued 
May 29, 2012, Officially Released.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Sullivan v. Lazzari, 305 Conn. 925, 47 A.3d 884, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 317 (Conn., July 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Summary process action, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Housing Session, where thecourt, Abrams, J., denied the defendants' motions to dismiss, to strike and for a jury trial; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Abrams, J., issued an articulation of its decision; thereafter, Christopher J. Donlin, administrator of the estate of Edith Fryer, was substituted as the party plaintiff, and the defendants filed an amended appeal.
Sullivan v. Lazzari, 303 Conn. 927, 35 A.3d 1075, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 43 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly denied defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiff's summary process action because the notice to quit complied with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-23(b). The notice identified the premises. Plaintiff's alleged failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47a-15a did not deprive the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction because that statute did not apply. The case did not concern unpaid rent or a rental agreement. If one of defendants' last names was misspelled on the notice to quit, that was a clerical error that did not deprive the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Caracoglia


AC 32699


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


134 Conn. App. 175; 38 A.3d 226; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 119


October 25, 2011, Argued 
March 13, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the infraction of creating a public disturbance, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, and tried to the court, Vitale, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction of two infractions of creating a public disturbance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181a(a)(1) and 53a-181a(a)(2) was affirmed. The infractions did not violate defendant's free speech rights under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. A judicial gloss was adopted such that defendant's predominant intent had to have been to cause inconvenience, annoyance or alarm, rather than to exercise his constitutional rights. By that gloss, § 53a-181a(a)(1) and 53a-181a(a)(2) were not facially vague.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

134 Conn. App. 124; 38 A.3d 191; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 108


November 30, 2011, Argued 
March 6, 2012, Officially Released

Action for, inter alia, a declaratory judgment determining whether Connecticut pretrial release statutes violate the state and federal constitutions, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Miller, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Hernandez v. Carbone, 567 F. Supp. 2d 320, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 57264 (D. Conn., 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The dismissal of plaintiff's suit seeking declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the pretrial release statutes, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-63a et seq., was affirmed. Ct. § 43-40 excluded certain periods from the time within which trial had to commence, and some detainees might choose to waive their speedy trial rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Boutilier

State v. Ayala

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


133 Conn. App. 514; 36 A.3d 274; 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 69


December 5, 2011, Argued 
February 14, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Ayala, 304 Conn. 913, 40 A.3d 318, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 140 (2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ayala v. Comm'r of Corr., 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 313 (Conn. App. Ct., Sept. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the second degree with a firearm, burglary in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree with a firearm, threatening in the second degree and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, and tried to the jury before B. Fischer, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support his kidnapping conviction. The appellate court held that although defendant did not physically restrain the victim during her confinement, the jury could have inferred, in light of his immediately prior threat against her life while he was armed with a deadly weapon, that an implicit threat still existed at the time that he ordered her to sit on the couch and, thus, it was reasonable for the jury to infer from his conduct that he possessed the specific intent to prevent the victim's liberation, even if only briefly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

February 7, 2012, Officially Released

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Fuger, J., rendered judgment dismissing the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Carter, 84 Conn. App. 263, 853 A.2d 565, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 335 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner filed a fourth petition for a writ of habeas corpus, claiming, inter alia, that his counsel had provided ineffective assistance. The habeas court rendered judgment dismissing the petition on the ground that the claims raised were barred by the doctrine of res judicata and were successive of claims raised in prior habeas petitions filed by the petitioner. The prisoner appealed. Because the prisoner's claim formed the basis of a distinct form of relief that he did not seek in any of his prior petitions, he was entitled to be heard in regard to that claim for relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part.

State v. Bonilla

131 Conn. App. 388; 28 A.3d 1005; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 469


June 1, 2011, Argued 
September 13, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of cruelty to animals and with the crime of gambling, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, where the court, Damiani, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to one count of cruelty to animals; subsequently, the state entered a nolle prosequi as to one count of cruelty to animals and as to the charge of gambling; judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

September 6, 2011, Officially Released.

Action to recover on a promissory note, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield where the court, Hon. Edward R. Karazin, Jr., judge trial referee, denied the defendants' motion to strike the plaintiff's prayer for relief; thereafter, the defendants filed a counterclaim, and the matter was transferred to the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, Complex Litigation Docket; subsequently, the court, Shay, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to strike the counterclaim; thereafter, the court, Shay, J., granted the defendants' motion to reargue and vacated in part its order striking count one of the counterclaim; subsequently, the court, Blawie, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment on the counterclaim, and the defendants appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, Blawie, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to preclude certain evidence and denied the defendants' motion to preclude certain evidence, and the matter was tried to the jury before the court, Blawie, J., on the complaint; verdict for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court, Blawie, J., denied the defendants' motion to set aside the verdict, and the defendants  [***2] filed a separate appeal to this court; thereafter, the court, Blawie, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, and the defendants appealed to this court and the plaintiff cross appealed.
Cadle Co. v. D'Addario, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 550 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 1, 2010)
Cadle Co. v. D'Addario, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1996 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 26, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditor sued defendants coexecutors under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-400 on a promissory note executed by their father. The appellate court held the coexecutors' motion to strike the creditor's prayer for relief was properly denied because, while Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-400 was a purely procedural statute that did not authorize a cause of action, the complaint alleged the coexecutors were liable for the note's principal amount and did not tender the sum due, and the prayer for relief stated the action was based on an express agreement to pay a definite sum, so it was legally sufficient.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.

State v. Alonzo


AC 30725


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


131 Conn. App. 1; 26 A.3d 109; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 453


May 17, 2011, Argued 
August 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Alonzo, 303 Conn. 912, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 515 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, assault in the first degree and assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Matasavage, J., granted the state's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the first degree and assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Alonzo, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1776 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 28, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: A judgment convicting defendant of assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-59(a)(1) and 53a-60(a)(2) was affirmed. A jury instruction requiring the jury to unanimously acquit defendant of first-degree assault before it could consider second-degree assault did not violate defendant's Conn. Const. art. I, § 19 right. The right to a jury trial did not encompass the court's jury instructions with regard to the process or manner of its deliberations. Not every feature of jury procedures as they existed in 1818 applied today. The procedural application of the right to a jury trial was malleable.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Affirmed by State v. Patterson, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 200 (Conn., June 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of risk of injury to a child and cruelty to persons, and with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Thompson, J.; judgment of guilty of two counts each of risk of injury to a child and cruelty to persons, and of the lesser included offense of criminally negligent homicide; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal or a new trial, and the defendant appealed to this court.

DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, judgment directed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:

OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part, affirmed in part, and remanded with direction.

State v. Henderson


AC 31610


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


130 Conn. App. 435; 24 A.3d 35; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 421


January 11, 2011, Argued 
August 2, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Henderson, 302 Conn. 938, 28 A.3d 992, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 437 (Oct. 4, 2011)
Appeal granted by, in part State v. Henderson, 302 Conn. 938, 28 A.3d 993, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 479 (Oct. 4, 2011)
Appeal dismissed by State v. Henderson, 308 Conn. 702, 66 A.3d 847, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 160 (June 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of assault in the third degree and with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, threatening, criminal mischief in the third degree and attempt to escape from custody, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender and a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendant was presented to the court, Espinosa, J., on a plea of guilty to the charge of criminal mischief in the third degree; thereafter, the remaining counts were tried to the jury; verdict of guilty of one count of assault in the third degree, robbery in the first degree, threatening and attempt to escape from custody; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which affirmed the trial court's judgment; thereafter, the court, Gold, J., dismissed the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant  [***2] appealed to this court.

OVERVIEW: The dismissal of defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence was affirmed. In re Probate Appeal of Cadle Co.


AC 31673


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


129 Conn. App. 814; 21 A.3d 572; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 377


November 17, 2010, Argued 
July 5, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Probate Appeal of Cadle Co., 302 Conn. 914, 27 A.3d 373, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 362 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two appeals from the decision of the Probate Court for the district of Trumbull, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield where the appeals were consolidated and tried to the court, Hon. L. Scott Melville, judge trial referee; judgments sustaining the appeals and remanding the cases to the Probate Court, for further proceedings, from which Cadle Company appealed to this court.
Cadle Co. v. D'Addario, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1368 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 1, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The judgments were reversed. The probate court had jurisdiction in ruling on an accounting in a decedent's estate to allow a creditor to conduct discovery into the management and operations of the estate's assets. Carten v. Carten, 219 A.2d 711 (Conn. 1966), was superseded by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-175(g). Under § 45a-175(g), the power of the probate court to order discovery in an accounting proceeding coincided with the power that a superior court judge would have had in a plenary case involving a challenge to such an account. The executors' interpretation of § 45a-175(g) was not plausible.


OUTCOME: Judgments reversed. Cases remanded to trial court with direction.

McKechnie v. McKechnie


AC 31498


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


130 Conn. App. 411; 23 A.3d 779; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 408


April 25, 2011, Argued 
July 26, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McKechnie v. McKechnie, 302 Conn. 931, 28 A.3d 345, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 388 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the defendant filed a cross complaint; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Gordon, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Gordon, J., issued an articulation of its decision; thereafter, the defendant withdrew his cross appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother said Conn. Gen. The mother could not succeed on this unpreserved claim, under Golding, because the statute's core clearly allowed a court to consider disability as long as disability was not a determinative factor in its decision, so the constitutional violation alleged by the mother was not clear.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT

519 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reynolds


AC 30776


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


126 Conn. App. 291; 11 A.3d 198; 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 38


September 20, 2010, Argued 
February 1, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of conspiracy to commit identity theft in the third degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the third degree, and, in the second part, with two counts of being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Bright, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to withdraw the plea and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Reynolds, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 483 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit identity theft in the third degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the third degree, he pleaded guilty to the part B information charging him as a persistent serious felony offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) denied his motion to withdraw his plea and sentenced defendant under § 53a-40(j). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant had knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to a jury trial. The record evidenced his full awareness of the nature of the charges, including the underlying larceny and identity theft as well as the enhancements sought for each. Nothing indicated that defendant was not of ordinary intelligence and educational background, and he had experience with the criminal justice system. The trial court permitted defendant, who represented himself, to consult with standby counsel at the hearing on the motion to withdraw the plea. The plea canvass met the standards for a knowing, intelligent and voluntary waiver. Defendant's plea of guilty operated as a waiver of his right to a jury trial not only with respect to whether he was a persistent serious felony offender but also with respect to whether his extended incarceration was in the public interest. The trial court had failed to make an explicit finding as to the public interest factor, requiring remand. The lack of such a finding, however, did not affect the voluntariness of the plea or provide grounds for withdrawal under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 39-27.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the part B information. It remanded the case for the trial court to find whether extended incarceration was in the public interest or for defendant to make the appropriate acknowledgement. Depending on that finding or acknowledgement, the trial court was to determine whether an enhanced sentence was appropriate. It affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

Buddington Park Condo. Ass'n v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


AC 31525


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


125 Conn. App. 724; 9 A.3d 426; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 585


October 19, 2010, Argued 
December 28, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Buddington Park Condo. Ass'n v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 300 Conn. 914, 13 A.3d 1101, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 88 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the named defendant approving the application by the defendant Carol Farrell et al. for a planned development district, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Hon. George W. Ripley II, judge trial referee; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Buddington Park Condo. v. Shelton Planning & Zoning, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1021 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 30, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a condominium association and others, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) dismissing their appeal from a decision of defendant planning and zoning commission. The condominium association claimed, inter alia, that it was denied due process when the commission received, ex parte, a revised site plan from defendant applicants following the close of the public hearing.


OVERVIEW: The applicants submitted an application for a planned development district to develop seven residential units on their property. The commission held hearings and conditionally voted to approve a resolution related to the application. The town planning consultant informed the commission that the staff had pointed out some geometric spacing problems to the applicants and the applicants provided a response as to how they could address those issues by removing one of the units down below bringing the number of units down to six, thereby addressing a number of other issues. The appellate court concluded that the commission received an ex parte communication from the applicants that it considered in approving the proposed district and that the court, therefore, improperly concluded that the condominium association had failed to demonstrate prejudice. The appellate court could not conclude that the commission's staff merely supplied technical information to the commission that it considered in approving the application. The information originated with the applicants. The consultant was a conduit. The association was prejudiced by the ex parte communication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to sustain the condominium association's appeal.

State v. Oral H.


AC 30289


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


125 Conn. App. 276; 7 A.3d 444; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 544


September 21, 2010, Argued 
November 30, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Oral H., 300 Conn. 902, 12 A.3d 573, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 48 (2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Oral H. v. Connecticut, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4487 (U.S., June 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with twenty-four counts of the crime of sexual assault in the third degree, and with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Schuman, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of twenty-four counts of sexual assault in the third degree and of sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) of 24 counts of sexual assault in the third degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2), and of sexual assault in the first degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1). He appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's victim was an adult. The appellate court held an information alleging Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2) violations was not dismissed due to the statute having been held unconstitutional when he was arrested, because Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. 84-3 stayed that holding until its reversal. An amendment adding a sexual assault in the first degree count did not offend separation of powers absent a probable cause finding because (1) nothing required this finding, and (2) defendant could not argue there was no probable cause after he was convicted. The State's decision to charge him, and not the victim, was not selective prosecution because (1) the State's charging decision was based on his history of controlling the victim, not his age or gender, and (2) it was no error to deny him an evidentiary hearing, as the court accepted the parties' factual representations and denied his motion to dismiss without prejudice. It was no error to admit expert testimony on delayed disclosure of sexual abuse without a Porter hearing because (1) such testimony was not scientific evidence requiring such a hearing, and (2) Connecticut had not extended Porter to other technical knowledge.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Hall v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 31377


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


124 Conn. App. 778; 6 A.3d 827; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 500


September 3, 2010, Argued 
November 2, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hall v. Comm'r of Corr., 299 Conn. 928, 12 A.3d 571, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 23 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
Hall v. Warden, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2273 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 16, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, Connecticut, which denied the inmate's amended petition for writ of habeas corpus and also denied his petition for certification to appeal. The inmate claimed that the habeas court abused its discretion when it concluded that he had received effective assistance from his trial counsel and that a guilty plea was voluntary, knowing and intelligent.


OVERVIEW: There was no abuse of discretion in the denial of the certificate to appeal or in the remainder of the habeas court's judgment. The habeas court correctly determined that the inmate did not prove that his defense was prejudiced by his trial counsel's failure to advise him regarding his parole eligibility. The record supported the habeas court's factual finding that the issue of parole eligibility did not play a part in and was not the centerpiece of any plea agreement that the inmate entered into with the State. The inmate's reliance on the Hernandez decision was misplaced. Contrary to the facts in Hernandez, the inmate's trial counsel did not misadvise the inmate as to his parole eligibility. As the issue of parole eligibility did not play a part in the inmate's decision to enter into the plea agreement, the habeas court correctly determined that the petitioner's plea was not rendered unintelligent, involuntary and unknowing due to the alleged ineffective assistance of his trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed the appeal.

 

523 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jay


AC 30002


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


124 Conn. App. 294; 4 A.3d 865; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 443


April 13, 2010, Argued 
October 5, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Jay, 299 Conn. 927, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 25 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of interfering with an officer, and with the crimes of evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and assault of public safety personnel, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, where the court, Strackbein, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court set aside the verdict of guilty of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and denied the defendant's motion for a new trial; judgment of guilty of two counts of interfering with an officer, and one count each of evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle and assault of public safety personnel, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, a jury convicted defendant of evasion of responsibility in the operation of a motor vehicle, assault of public safety personnel, and interfering with an officer. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one (Connecticut) imposed a total effective sentence of four years, suspended after 18 months, followed by three years probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, as the police entered his home without a warrant, in the absence of exigent circumstances. The appellate court found no error, noting that defendant failed to demonstrate that his conviction was tainted by any fruity of the alleged unlawful entry. The conduct underlying defendant's convictions occurred well after the time of the police entry; by the time of their commission, the police had identified themselves, announced the purpose of their presence, and emergency medical personnel had arrived. In addition, even if defendant could prevail on his claim of illegal entry, the evidence with regard to the crimes of interfering with an officer and assault of public safety personnel was admissible under the new crime exception. Defendant's challenge to the jury instructions also failed, as none of the instructions misled the jury or deprived defendant of his right to a jury trial. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant's conviction for assault of public safety personnel and interfering with an officer did not violate the protection against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Figueroa v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 28555


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


123 Conn. App. 862; 3 A.3d 202; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 395


October 27, 2009, Argued 
September 21, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Figueroa v. Comm'r of Corr., 299 Conn. 926, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 22 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Swords, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
State v. Figueroa, 74 Conn. App. 165, 166 Conn. App. 165, 810 A.2d 319, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 625 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who had been convicted of murder and carrying a pistol or revolver without a permit (Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a and 29-35, respectively), filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) granted the motion to dismiss filed by respondent commissioner of correction and denied the inmate's subsequent petition for certification to appeal. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate maintained that the amendments to §§ 53a-54a and 29-35 were void because the enactment clause required by Conn. Const. art. III, § 1 was omitted from the public acts that amended the statutes. Therefore, he argued, his conviction was void. The appellate court disagreed. He conflated the requirement of art. III, § 1, with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-58, the statutory provision requiring publication of public acts. Art. III, § 1, required that laws enacted by the legislature be prefaced by this clause: "Be it enacted by the Senate and House of Representatives in General Assembly convened." As the actual bills passed by the legislature contained the required enactment clause, there was no constitutional infirmity due to the lack of that prefatory language in the published versions. The failure to include the enactment clause in the published public acts did not deprive the inmate of notice of the nature of the charges against him. Information as to what acts §§ 53a-54a and 29-35 prohibited was available to the inmate by virtue of their publication under the authority of § 2-58, even without the inclusion of the enactment clause in the published volumes of the public acts.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

525 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pettigrew


AC 29405


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


124 Conn. App. 9; 3 A.3d 148; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 398


April 19, 2010, Argued 
September 21, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Pettigrew, 299 Conn. 916, 10 A.3d 1052, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 483 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, attempt to sell narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, conspiracy to sell narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project and attempt to sell narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to sell narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Kavanewsky, J., granted the state's motion for joinder; thereafter, the state filed a substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of conspiracy to distribute narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy to distribute narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project, and with the crimes of attempt to distribute narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and attempt to distribute narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project; subsequently,  [***2] the court, Pavia, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss or to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Pavia, J.; verdict and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), for various drug-related crimes, including conspiracy to distribute narcotics. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly consolidated two separate cases against him for trial, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b) was unconstitutionally vague, and his multiple sentences for conspiracy violated double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: The charges stemmed from two separate incidents. In the first incident, the officers used a taxicab and cellular telephone to arrange for the purchase of the narcotics from defendant, who was arrested when he approached the taxicab. The police recovered crack cocaine and cash. In the second incident, the police observed defendant conduct a drug sale. The appellate court held that a review of the transcripts revealed that the evidence was presented in a reasonably clear order, although it was not strictly chronological. When ruling on the motion for joinder, the court reasonably could have concluded that the case would not be particularly lengthy or complex. When considered as a whole, the charge presented the case to the jury so that no injustice would result. It was not reasonably possible that the charge, when read as a whole, impermissibly misled the jury to believe that it could consider all the evidence collectively when deciding each case. A person of ordinary intelligence would know that the act of "agreeing to distribute drugs while in the protected area" was illegal. Defendant was convicted of conspiracy because the jury concluded that all of the elements existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the sentences on the four conspiracy offenses. The case was remanded with direction to merge the convictions on the two conspiracy offenses in each case and to vacate the sentence for one of them. The judgments were affirmed in all other respects.

 

526 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kenney v. Weaving


AC 31227


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


123 Conn. App. 211; 1 A.3d 1083; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 381


May 20, 2010, Argued 
August 10, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Weaving, 125 Conn. App. 41, 6 A.3d 203, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 516 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Sheedy, J., granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant Robert M. Ward and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix of a decedent's estate sued defendants driver and commissioner, seeking damages for the decedent's death in a traffic accident. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) granted the commissioner's motion to dismiss. The administratrix appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died from injuries suffered when a car operated by the driver struck him. The administratrix alleged that, because of the driver's multiple convictions for driving under the influence, the commissioner was required to permanently revoke his license. The administratrix also alleged that the commissioner, through his acts or omissions, allowed the driver to maintain a valid driver's license, and to register operate his car. The trial court found that the action was barred by sovereign immunity. The appellate court found that this was proper. Among other things, the state clearly was the real party in interest. Damages were sought for injuries allegedly caused by the commissioner for performing or not performing acts that were part of his official duties. Clearly, the commissioner was sued only because of his official position at the time of the accident. The Supreme Court of Connecticut had explicitly rejected the argument that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 waived the state's sovereign immunity. Because the administratrix sought only monetary damages, costs, and punitive damages, the exception for actions by officers in excess of their statutory authority did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Deas v. Diaz


AC 31143


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 826; 998 A.2d 200; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 340


March 8, 2010, Argued 
June 22, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Deas v. Diaz, 298 Conn. 905, 3 A.3d 69, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 315 (2010)
Subsequent appeal at Deas v. Diaz, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 539 (Conn. App. Ct., Nov. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, personal injuries sustained as a result of the defendants' alleged negligence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the defendant Transportation General, Inc., filed a counterclaim; thereafter, the named defendant et al., were defaulted for failure to appear; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury before Corradino, J.; thereafter, the court sustained the plaintiffs objection to the introduction of certain evidence; verdict for the plaintiff on the complaint and for the defendant Transportation General, Inc., on the counterclaim; subsequently, the court denied the motions filed by the defendant Transportation General, Inc., to set aside the verdict and for remittitur, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant Transportation General, Inc., appealed to this court.
Deas v. Diaz, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1319 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 12, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxi driver sued defendants, a taxicab company and the driver and the owner of a vehicle. A jury found defendant driver and the owner 20 percent negligent and the company, on the basis of plaintiff's uninsured motorist (UM) claim, 80 percent negligent; it awarded plaintiff damages. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, Connecticut, denied the company's motions to set aside the verdict and for remittitur; it appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff's taxi was struck by a vehicle driven by defendant driver, who had swerved to avoid a van that had veered into his lane. Plaintiff, an independent contractor, brought the UM claim against the company because the van's owner could not be found. The company argued that the jury's award of non-economic damages and future economic damages should have been set aside as excessive under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-216a. The appellate court disagreed. Applying a plenary standard of review, it found that testimony that plaintiff, then 29, would incur $ 1000 to $ 2000 per year in medical care; that he continued to experience pain and trouble sleeping; and that his spine was compromised and would never return to its pre-injury status, supported the trial court's finding that the damage award was not excessive as a matter of law. The jury reasonably could have determined that a release plaintiff signed was not enforceable due to the company's superior bargaining power, or for one of the other reasons set forth in the jury instructions. The trial court properly excluded statements about plaintiff made by an unknown ambulance driver, as they were unreliable and unduly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nasheed


AC 29661


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 672; 997 A.2d 623; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 283


December 3, 2009, Argued 
June 15, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Nasheed, 298 Conn. 902, 3 A.3d 73, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 323 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, larceny in the second degree and assault in the third degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter the defendant was tried to the court on the second part of the information; judgment of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), defendant was convicted of first degree robbery, second degree larceny, and third degree assault. After a bench trial, he was convicted of being a persistent dangerous felony offender (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a)(1) (2007)) and was sentenced to a total effective term of 40 years' incarceration. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that admitting hearsay testimony from his former probation officer during the bench trial violated his U.S. Const. amend. VI rights to confrontation under Crawford. The appellate court held that as most of what she testified about--defendant's robbery convictions, use of a gun during those crimes, receipt of disciplinary tickets, and positive drug tests while on probation--were corroborated by his own testimony, any error in admitting this evidence was harmless. The evidence was sufficient to prove that he was a persistent dangerous felony offender and that his history and the circumstances of his crimes indicated that extended incarceration and lifetime supervision would best serve the public interest (§ 53a-40(h)). Section 53a-40(h) was not unconstitutionally vague, either as applied to him or on its face. Even assuming the prosecutor improperly characterized the evidence during closing argument, defendant was not deprived of a fair trial as the trial court's instructions that the jury was the sole finder of fact and that arguments made during summation were not facts were sufficient to cure any alleged impropriety, and the evidence of guilt was strong.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Adorno


AC 30484


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 534; 996 A.2d 746; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 253


February 2, 2010, Argued 
June 8, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Adorno, 297 Conn. 929, 998 A.2d 1196, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 284 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree and with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham at Danielson, where the matter was tried to the jury before Fuger, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to admit certain evidence; verdict of guilty of three counts of risk of injury to a child and two counts of sexual assault in the fourth degree; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions to set aside the verdict and for a new trial, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham at Danielson (Connecticut), after the denial of his motions to admit evidence of the victim's sexual history under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86f and to set aside the verdict and for a new trial, of sexual assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A) (2005) and risk of injury to a child under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that it was error to exclude evidence as to the victim's sexual history as defendant theorized that the victim lied about the sexual assault in order to cover up the possibility that her boyfriend was the source of any infection that a medical examination might have revealed. The evidence was relevant to the first-degree sexual assault charge, but defendant was acquitted on that charge. A new trial was required on a risk of injury charge that stemmed from the sexual assault charge. The victim's sexual relationship with her boyfriend was not relevant to understanding the victim's motive, bias, or interest on the other counts. The exclusion of irrelevant evidence did not infringe on defendant's rights of confrontation and to present evidence. It was not error to exclude two clinic employees' testimony that the victim had given inconsistent statements. While the jury instruction on § 53-21(a)(2) improperly defined likely, accurate instructions minimized any harm. Defendant was convicted of the sexual assault and subjected the minor victim to sexual contact. It was difficult to imagine a finding that sexual contact was not likely to impair the victim's morals.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed only as to the conviction of risk of injury to a child, and the case was remanded for a new trial on that charge only. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

In re Jazmine B.


AC 30390


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 376; 996 A.2d 286; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 211


February 2, 2010, Argued 
May 25, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Jazmine B., 297 Conn. 924, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 301 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Juvenile Matters, and tried to the court, Kahn, J.; judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent father appealed to this court.
In re Jazmine Marie B., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1404 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 13, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed the termination of his parental rights by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) with respect to his minor daughter. The father claimed that the trial court erroneously found that he had failed to achieve a sufficient degree of personal rehabilitation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) and improperly terminated his parental rights as § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The father had an extensive criminal history, including manslaughter, threatening, assault, and risk of injury to a child. Despite a licensed psychologist's opinion that it was in the child's best interest to stay with her foster family, the trial court ordered specific steps toward reunification. After a visit, the child accused the father of sexual abuse. Petitioner Department of Children and Families filed a petition for the termination of the father's and the mother's parental rights. While the father completed parenting classes, as he failed to engage in individual therapy and/or sexual offender treatment to enable him to reunify with the child, the trial court found he was unable to address the emotional and physical needs of his child. The appellate court held it was not clearly erroneous for the court to find that the Department was justified in referring the father to sexual offender treatment. The trial court also had sufficient evidence before it to conclude that the Department had begun the process of referring the father to individual counseling, which he preemptively refused. Thus, it properly found that he had failed to achieve sufficient personal rehabilitation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Fisher


AC 29519


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 335; 995 A.2d 105; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 207


December 1, 2009, Argued 
May 25, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Iannotti, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; judgment revoking the defendant's probation; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a new trial, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Fisher, 52 Conn. App. 825, 729 A.2d 229, 1999 Conn. App. LEXIS 137 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the revocation of his probation by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32. Defendant claims that the trial court impermissibly restricted his cross-examination of a witness and violated his Sixth Amendment right to Confrontation. Alternatively, he argued that the trial court improperly failed to draw a negative inference from the absence of a 911 recording.


OVERVIEW: Some time after his release from incarceration and the commencement of his term of probation, defendant moved to New York City. The police received a 911 telephone call. The caller reported that a nude man was on the stoop masturbating. The witness later testified that he saw a white lotion on defendant's hands. The police officers examined defendant's residence and observed a trail of droplets of a "white liquid" and a silver dollar sized "dollop" of the white liquid just inside the door on the floor. Defendant argued that the failure to disclose a recording of the 911 call infringed upon his right of confrontation. The appellate court noted that the State never had possession of a recording of the 911 call as one never existed. Thus, there was no violation of the right of confrontation. The trial court provided a lengthy and detailed analysis of its reasoning behind imposing the sentence. The totality of the circumstances gave no indication that the trial court improperly augmented defendant's sentence on the basis of his decision to exercise his privilege to remain silent.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Lavigne


AC 29098


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 190; 995 A.2d 94; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 196


December 7, 2009, Argued 
May 18, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Lavigne, 298 Conn. 909, 4 A.3d 835, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 343 (2010)
Affirmed by State v. Lavigne, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 495 (Conn., Dec. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with five counts each of the crimes of larceny in the first degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, and tried to the jury before Fuger, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal; verdict of guilty of one count of larceny in the second degree; subsequently, the court declared a mistrial as to five counts of larceny in the first degree and four counts of larceny in the second degree, and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Lavigne v. Loulakis, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 421 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 19, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) of larceny by embezzlement from a person who was 60 years of age or older under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123(a)(5), after a mistrial was declared as to nine remaining counts, and her sentence of five years of imprisonment, execution suspended after six months, five years of probation, and restitution of $ 3307.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the evidence supported the conviction. The State showed that defendant made withdrawals totalling $ 3307 from a joint account with the ward. There was sufficient evidence that defendant knew that the victim's assets were under the control of the conservator, that she had been notified of her duty to report to the conservator all accounts held by the ward, whether they were sole or joint accounts, and that she did not do so. There was sufficient evidence that defendant withdrew the $ 3307 from the joint bank accounts with wrongful intent. The jury instructions were proper. The question of defendant's actual ownership right to funds as a joint account holder was a fact question for the jury. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123(a)(5) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied because defendant was charged with embezzling from a ward's estate. It is not the form in which the property was held, but to whom it belonged that was determinative of a § 53a-123(a) offense. Section 53a-123(a)(5) afforded defendant sufficient notice that it applied to conduct that occurred after a conservator had been appointed for the ward's estate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Earl B.


AC 30491


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 269; 994 A.2d 713; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 203


November 17, 2009, Argued 
May 18, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by In re Earl B., 297 Conn. 921, 996 A.2d 1192, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 264 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for an adjudication of delinquency, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters, where the court, B. Kaplan, J., adjudicated the respondent a delinquent and committed him to the custody of the commissioner of children and families; thereafter, the court, Brown, J., denied the respondent's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the respondent appealed to this court.
Earl B. v. Comm'r of Children & Families, 288 Conn. 163, 952 A.2d 32, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 297 (2008)
State v. Sargeant, 288 Conn. 673, 954 A.2d 839, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 352 (2008)
State v. Foreman, 288 Conn. 684, 954 A.2d 135, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 353 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), adjudicated respondent juvenile a delinquent and committed him, pursuant to an agreed on sentence, to the custody of the commissioner of children and families. Thereafter, the trial court denied respondent's motion to correct an illegal sentence. Respondent appealed, arguing the court exceeded its statutory authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-140(i).


OVERVIEW: The State negotiated a plea agreement in which respondent pleaded guilty to a serious juvenile offense. As part of respondent's agreed on sentence, the trial court issued a separate order for 42 months of banishment from a specific county. The banishment order had expired, and the parties conceded respondent's appeal was moot. In further analysis, respondent's claim did not qualify for review under the "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception. The banishment order was not a condition of respondent's four year commitment to the commissioner, not a component of the treatment plan devised by the commissioner, nor subject to review and modification every six months. It was a separate order entered by the trial court pursuant to the parties' agreement during respondent's delinquency adjudication. As such, it was subject to challenge on direct appeal or pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 43-22. Respondent did not bring a direct appeal or prompt challenge to the order. Respondent's claim became moot because of his delay, not because the banishment order was by its very nature limited in duration or presented a functionally insurmountable time constraint.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Bewry v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 30505


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


121 Conn. App. 259; 994 A.2d 697; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 199


February 8, 2010, Argued 
May 18, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Bewry v. Comm'r of Corr., 297 Conn. 918, 996 A.2d 277, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 252 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the matter was tried to the court, A. Santos, J.; judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court.
Bewry v. Warden, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 584 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 12, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the denial by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) of his petition for certification to appeal the denial of his habeas petition based on ineffective assistance by counsel in his two trials, his two direct appeals, his first habeas, and the appeal from his first habeas, for their failure to raise a claim that his arraignment was untimely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-1g (1987).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that after the inmate sustained injuries on September 6, 1988, he was taken to the hospital for treatment. He was discharged from the hospital and arrested on Saturday, September 17, 1988. The inmate was arraigned on Monday, September 19, 1988. The inmate did not show that a warrant issued for his arrest that was sworn on September 9, 1988, was executed before his discharge. The inmate could not have been arraigned on a Saturday, and was properly arraigned on Monday. The arraignment was not delayed past the first possible opportunity for the State to bring him before a judge. Further, § 54-1g was not contravened even if the inmate had been arrested during his hospitalization as the police were not free to remove him and have him arraigned until the hospital staff determined that he medically was able to be discharged. Connecticut did not provide for in-hospital arraignments. The inmate was arraigned as the first regular sitting of the trial court following his return to police custody. Prior counsel did not provide deficient performance, and the inmate was not prejudiced. The inmate was properly denied certification to appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Mourning v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 30744


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


120 Conn. App. 612; 992 A.2d 1169; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 155


January 4, 2010, Argued 
April 27, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mourning v. Comm'r of Corr., 297 Conn. 919, 996 A.2d 1192, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 260 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, T. Santos, J., granted the respondent's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Mourning v. Warden, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2514 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 2, 2008)



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-466, claiming insufficient proof of probation violations. Respondent, the Commissioner of Correction, filed a motion to dismiss, arguing the inmate was no longer in custody on the probation violations. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) granted the motion. Upon being granted certification, the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1996, the inmate was convicted of three offenses and sent to prison. After his release, the inmate was arrested and charged with one count of sale of narcotics and three counts of violation of probation, resulting from his 1996 convictions. The trial court terminated the probations, accepted the inmate's guilty plea to sale of narcotics, and sentenced him on that charge to a term of imprisonment. The inmate, acting as a self-represented party, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus and later amended the petition. The inmate argued the habeas court failed to construe his amended petition as a challenge to his current conviction for sale of narcotics. The inmate's passing reference to his 2007 arrest in his amended petition could not be read as an attack on his resulting sentence on that charge, even under the most liberal reading of the petitions. The habeas court properly construed the original and amended petitions together as contesting only the findings that the inmate violated his probation and not on his present sentence for sale of narcotics. The inmate did not preserve the claim that the habeas court failed to construe his petitions as a writ of error coram nobis.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court was affirmed.
