State v. Staton


AC 29607


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


120 Conn. App. 497; 992 A.2d 348; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 135


February 4, 2010, Argued 
April 20, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Staton, 297 Conn. 911, 995 A.2d 640, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 273 (2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Staton v. Warden, State Prison, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 265 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 9, 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Stay denied by, Motion denied by, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Staton v. Brighthaupt, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47795 (D. Conn., Apr. 4, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of narcotics, sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics, possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school and loitering in or about school grounds, and, in the second part, with having previously been convicted of possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Thim, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Iannotti, J.; verdict of guilty of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of narcotics, sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics and possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court, Reynolds, J., on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of narcotics, sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics, and possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to twenty years in prison, execution suspended after twelve years, and five years of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence, because the police lacked a sufficient reasonable suspicion of criminal conduct and his subsequent detention by police was unconstitutionally prolonged. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the police had reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigative stop. Among other things, the police were on the lookout for suspicious activity associated with a brown car with Colorado license plates. After a car matching that description stopped in front of a school, defendant suddenly appeared, leaned into the car, and walked away 20 seconds later. The trial court cited to the officer's 20 plus years of experience in determining whether he possessed a reasonable and articulable suspicion to detain defendant. The appellate court also found that the 12 to 15 detention of defendant was not illegal, but was tied to, and justified by, the circumstances that gave rise to the officer's reasonable and articulable suspicion that defendant was involved in a drug transaction. The detection allowed an officer to pursue the vehicle, search it, and have defendant identify a passenger.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Moulton


AC 29617


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


120 Conn. App. 330; 991 A.2d 728; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 139


April 15, 2009, Argued 
April 13, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Moulton, 297 Conn. 916, 996 A.2d 278, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 245 (2010)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Remanded by State v. Moulton, 2013 Conn. LEXIS 348 (Conn., Oct. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of breach of the peace in the second degree and harassment in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of second degree breach of the peace and second degree harassment. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one (Connecticut) sentenced him to six months, suspended, and two years probation for breach of peace, and 90 days, suspended, and one year probation for harassment, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose out a phone call to her place of employment, a post office. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that her conviction for harassment had to be reversed because application of the harassment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(3), to her phone conversation implicated her rights under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The appellate court agreed, finding that, while the statute on its face did not infringe on defendant's freedom on speech, it was unconstitutional as applied because defendant was punished for the verbal content of her phone call and not the actual making of the call. Defendant also claimed that the trial court improperly instructed the jury. The appellate court agreed as to the breach of peace charge, but not as to the harassment charge. As to the breach of peace charge, the trial court should have instructed the jury to consider the factual context in which the allegedly threatening conduct occurred. The appellate court found the evidence sufficient to support the breach of peace charge, thereby permitted a retrial on that charge, but insufficient to support the harassment charge, necessitating an acquittal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial on the breach of peace charge and with direction to render a judgment of not guilty on the harassment charge.

Williams v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 29528


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


120 Conn. App. 412; 991 A.2d 705; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 147


January 11, 2010, Argued 
April 13, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Williams v. Comm'r of Corr., 295 Conn. 915, 297 Conn. 915, 996 A.2d 279, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 247 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the Williams v. Commissioner of Correction granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Williams v. Warden, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3134 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut) denied the petition. The inmate appealed. Pursuant to a plea agreement, the inmate previously pled guilty to possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell, larceny in the third degree, and assault in the third degree. The plea on the assault charge was vacated.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's claim that trial counsel was ineffective because he provided erroneous legal advice, including incorrect information on the possible sentence, causing the inmate to enter unknowing, unintelligent, and involuntary guilty pleas failed, because the court was clear in going over the terms of the plea agreement with the inmate and the inmate was clear that he understood those terms. While the appellate court found that counsel was ineffective for providing the inmate with incorrect information regarding the maximum possible sentence the inmate was facing, the inmate failed to prove that, absent such incorrect information, he would have insisted on going to trial. The inmate also claimed that counsel failed to attend most of court hearing and did not engage in ongoing meaningful plea negotiations. The inmate could not prove that counsel was rendered ineffective assistance as to plea negotiations, as the inmate was facing nearly 40 on the charges that could have moved forward and up to 65 years if the information were amended to conform to the evidence, but counsel secured a sentence of nine years, suspended after four, with five years probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court was affirmed.

 

539 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Booker v. Jarjura


AC 29940, AC 29941


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


120 Conn. App. 1; 990 A.2d 894; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 105


October 15, 2009, Argued 
March 23, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Booker v. Jarjura, 297 Conn. 909, 995 A.2d 636, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 209 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for, inter alia, quo warranto challenging the appointment of the defendant Dov Braunstein et al. to positions on certain commissions of the city of Waterbury, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the action was withdrawn as against the defendant Nancy Howse; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Cremins, J.; judgment in part for the plaintiff, from which the plaintiff and the defendant Dov Braunstein filed separate appeals to this court, which consolidated the appeals.
Booker v. Jarjura, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1115 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 2, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a minority leader for a city board of aldermen (ML), appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which was granted in part for him in his quo warranto and mandamus action, wherein he challenged the appointment of defendant commissioner to certain city commission positions by defendants, a mayor and a zoning commission (ZC). The commissioner also appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mayor had the duty to appoint city electors to various boards and commissions pursuant to Waterbury, Conn., Charter Chapter 4, § 4-2. Although the ML provided names of suggested electors to be appointed, others were appointed by either the mayor or the ZC for various commissions. The ML challenged those appointments. The trial court granted a writ of quo warranto and ordered the ouster of one commissioner. However, it denied the same relief as to another commissioner, and it denied a request for mandamus relief against the ZC. On appeal, the court reviewed the Waterbury, Conn., Charter and found that the trial court had interpreted it correctly. The restriction on the mayor's appointment under § 4-2(b)(1) was not applicable to appointments by, inter alia, the ZC under § 4-2(b)(2). Accordingly, denial of the quo warranto as to the ZC's appointment was proper. Based on that same reasoning, a writ of mandamus against the ZC was properly denied. As to the grant of quo warranto with respect to one commissioner, the court found that the mayor's failure to adhere to the restrictions under § 4-2(b)(1) necessitated that relief. Section 4-2(b)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Kurzatkowski


AC 29610


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


119 Conn. App. 556; 988 A.2d 393; 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 68


October 22, 2009, Argued 
March 2, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Kurzatkowski, 296 Conn. 902, 991 A.2d 1104, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 156 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault of a peace officer, interfering with an officer, failure to stop a motor vehicle when signaled, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and reckless driving, and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender and with having previously been convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Dolan, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of nolo contendere to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Connecticut, defendant was convicted of, inter alia, assault of a peace officer (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c(a)(1)) and interfering with an officer (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a(a)). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: When an officer approached defendant's car he accelerated and almost hit the officer. A second officer pursued defendant. He fled from his car and fought with the officer, who testified that he sustained pain, bloody knees, and injuries to his ankle and Achilles tendon. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to prove he had the specific intent to injure the officer or that the officer was injured by him. The appellate court disagreed. The requisite intent under § 53a-167c was the intent to prevent the officer from performing his duties, not to injure him; the evidence was sufficient to prove that intent and that defendant's actions were a proximate cause of the injuries. The jury was properly instructed on specific intent. As an instruction on intervening cause was not warranted by the evidence, failing to give it was not error. Section 53a-167c(a)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided fair warning that a specific intent to injure an officer was not an element of the offense. Under State v. Mincewicz, defendant's convictions of both interfering with an officer and assault of a peace officer violated the double jeopardy ban on multiple punishments.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for interfering with an officer was vacated and his conviction on that charge was combined with his conviction of assault of a peace officer; the case was remanded for resentencing. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Manson


AC 27561


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


118 Conn. App. 538; 984 A.2d 1099; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 538


October 13, 2009, Argued 
December 22, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Manson, 295 Conn. 902, 988 A.2d 878, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 60 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and with the crimes of burglary in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Mullarkey, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Manson, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3351 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 27, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, one count of burglary in the first degree, and one count of unlawful restraint in the first degree. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to a total effective sentence of 45 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the photo array identification made by the victim because the victim did not make a definitive identification of defendant's photo until shown a second array with defendant's photo repeated and the victim could not reliably identify defendant. The appellate court found no error, noting that the trial court found that the police used eight photos in the array, the array was composed of individuals who strongly resembled defendant, no suggestion was made to the victim that a photo of the suspected perpetrator was in the array, and no verbal or physical hints were given by police. The fact that defendant's photo was in both arrays was not unconstitutionally suggestive in defendant's case, as the entire array was repeated. The appellate court also found no error in the exclusion of defendant's proffered expert on identification testimony, as the expert had no special expertise with respect to identifications by the elderly or sexual assault victims. Finally, the appellate court found no possibility that the jury was misled by the challenged jury instruction on the elements of burglary.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Ware v. State


AC 28600


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


118 Conn. App. 65; 983 A.2d 853; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 501; 107 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1498


April 27, 2009, Argued 
November 24, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the allegedly wrongful termination of the plaintiff's employment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Hon. Richard M. Rittenband, judge trial referee, denied the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Ware v. State, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 115 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 16, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee, claiming she was terminated due to her pregnancy, sued defendant State of Connecticut for wrongful termination, employment discrimination in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60, and breach of contract. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford, Connecticut, denied the State's motion to dismiss. The State filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that plaintiff's wrongful termination and breach of contract claims were barred by sovereign immunity. The appellate court agreed. Plaintiff's employment was not governed by the Connecticut Personnel Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-193 et seq., as she contended, but by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-12, under which the judiciary promulgated its own personnel policies, and § 51-12 did not expressly or impliedly waive the State's sovereign immunity. As her employment was governed only by § 51-12, and not by any implied contract, her breach of contract claim failed. The State's waiver of sovereign immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100 was conditioned on plaintiff's exhausting her administrative remedies with the Connecticut Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities. As she did not satisfy the exhaustion requirement as to claims brought under § 46a-60(a)(4) and (5), she could not obtain, as to those claims, a release of jurisdiction pursuant to § 46a-100 and, therefore, was not entitled to take advantage of the State's statutory waiver of sovereign immunity. Finally, sovereign immunity barred plaintiff's request for punitive damages under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-104.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

McCook v. Whitebirch Constr., LLC


AC 30144


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


117 Conn. App. 320; 978 A.2d 1150; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 433


June 3, 2009, Argued 
September 29, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McCook v. Whitebirch Constr., LLC, 294 Conn. 932, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 47 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action, in the first case, to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract, and for other relief, and actions, in the second and third cases, to foreclose mechanic's liens on certain of the named defendant's real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Peck, J., granted the motions filed by the plaintiffs in the second and third cases to enforce the parties' settlement agreement and rendered judgments accordingly, from which the named defendant in the second and third cases appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a judgment entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which granted the motions to enforce a settlement agreement brought by defendants, a general contractor and a lumber company, which settled three related civil actions, and awarded the contractor interest and attorney's fees arising from its motion to enforce the agreement.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that checks submitted by the owner to support a fraud claim were not relevant to whether the parties agreed on the terms in the settlement, and whether those terms were sufficiently clear at the time of the settlement. The terms of the agreement were clear and unambiguous. The owner admitted that, at the time of the settlement, he believed that all three cases were being settled in the agreement. The owner's testimony that he did not think the settlement included his Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act claim was not credible. The owner's claim that attorney's fees and interest were improperly awarded was not preserved for appeal. The claim that the trial court improperly denied the owner's motion to articulate its reasons for denying his motion to reconsider was not reviewable on appeal because the owner failed to pursue his remedies under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. §§ 66-5 and 66-7. The owner's claim that he was denied his right to be heard under the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 because the parties were not canvassed to ensure that they understood the terms of the settlement agreement was rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

State v. Hayward


AC 29709


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


116 Conn. App. 511; 976 A.2d 791; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 363


May 29, 2009, Argued 
August 18, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hayward, 293 Conn. 934, 981 A.2d 1077, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 466 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, and tried to the jury before Vitale, J.; verdict of guilty of one count of assault in the second degree; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Hayward, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2008 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 23, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three (Connecticut), convicted defendant of second degree assault, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60(a)(2). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of defendant's attack on his girlfriend. Defendant argued that, because the weapon used was not in evidence and the victim testified that she did not know what caused her injuries, there was insufficient evidence that the weapon was a dangerous instrument under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-3(7). The appellate court found that the evidence showed that the victim was seriously disfigured, and had scarring from the injuries inflicted by defendant. The jury reasonably could have found that the lacerations and the resulting scarring on the victim's nose amounted to a serious disfigurement. According to the victim's treating physician, the cut to her nose was most likely caused by a sharp object. The victim told police that she had been cut with an object, possibly a knife. The jury reasonably could have inferred that defendant used a dangerous instrument in the attack, capable of causing serious disfigurement or serious physical injury and that it in fact caused such injury. Statements made by the prosecutor in closing argument were improper, but defendant did not satisfy the severity prong of the Thompson standard. Further, the State's case was strong.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Bivrell


AC 29860


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


116 Conn. App. 556; 976 A.2d 60; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 365


June 2, 2009, Argued 
August 18, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bivrell, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 100 (Conn., Mar. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault of an elderly person in the third degree and breach of the peace in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Keegan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield, Connecticut, of third degree assault of an elderly person (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61a) and second degree breach of the peace (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(2)). She appealed.


OVERVIEW: The 71-year-old victim testified that defendant, while wearing a ring, struck him several times in the head, causing bleeding, ringing in his ear, confusion, disorientation, and hearing loss. The appellate court held that as the jury could have inferred from the victim's testimony that he was in pain due to the beating and that defendant intended to injure him, the evidence supported defendant's conviction of third degree assault of an elderly person. As the jury reasonably could have inferred that by assaulting the victim, defendant further intended to "cause inconvenience, annoyance or alarm, or recklessly created a risk thereof," the evidence supported her conviction of second degree breach of the peace. Defendant's claim that the trial court improperly diluted the State's burden of proof by charging the jury not to be swayed by sympathy was meritless, as the instruction the trial court gave had been previously found to be proper. As the State, and not defendant, requested a charge on the lesser included offense of assault in the third degree, defendant failed to satisfy the first prong of State v. Whistnant and thus was not entitled to a lesser included offense charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Elson


AC 28007


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


116 Conn. App. 196; 975 A.2d 678; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 353


December 10, 2008, Argued 
August 4, 2009, Officially Released*


* The defendant's motion for reconsideration and reargument en banc was granted by this court on September 3, 2009. Part V of this opinion has been superseded by State v. Elson, 125 Conn. App.328, ___ A.2d ___ (2010).


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 8, 2010.
Superseded by, in part, On reconsideration by, En banc State v. Elson, 125 Conn. App. 328, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 545 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault in the first degree, attempt to commit assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, and, in the second part, with having committed an offense while on release, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Schuman, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal; verdict of guilty of assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree; subsequently, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the defendant filed an amended appeal with this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed jury convictions from a trial court (Connecticut) for assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1) and unlawful restraint in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95(a), as alleged in Part A information. The trial court also found defendant guilty of committing an offense while on pretrial release in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40b(1), as alleged in a part B information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of assaulting a female student with fists and a knife in a college classroom, inflicting serious injuries. On appeal, the court held that defendant waived his argument that the trial court improperly instructed the jury that defendant's bare hands were dangerous instruments for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1). The court properly admitted into evidence a facsimile of a serrated knife that the state argued that he used during the attack because the parties jointly stipulated to its admission in order to avoid admitting a knife found in defendant's car that was stained with a red substance. The facsimile was relevant to explain the origin of the victim's injuries, even though it was larger than the knife the victim described. Jury instructions did not improperly comment on defendant's self-interest in the outcome of the trial or on the state's interest in protecting innocent persons from being convicted of crimes. The instruction on reasonable doubt was not constitutionally infirm. The evidence was sufficient to show that the victim was seriously injured, an element of first-degree assault, and that defendant intended to cause such injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Maurice M.


AC 29557


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


116 Conn. App. 1; 975 A.2d 90; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 290


February 3, 2009, Argued 
July 28, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Maurice M., 293 Conn. 926, 980 A.2d 913, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 408 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Maurice M., 2011 Conn. LEXIS 464 (Conn., Nov. 29, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, and tried to the court, T. Sullivan, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, T. Sullivan, J., issued an articulation of its decision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) revoked defendant's probation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32 following defendant's arrest on a charge of risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1). It reinstated his original one-year prison sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was watching television when his two-year-old wandered out into the street and was nearly hit by a vehicle. The court first held that § 53-21(a)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant. Lawful behavior that presented a foreseeable risk of injury to a child fell under the purview of § 53-21(a)(1). Here, although the conduct at issue was otherwise lawful, a reasonable person would recognize that allowing a two-year-old child to play unsupervised in a home situated near a busy street, with an unlocked back door and no child safety devices, presented a foreseeable risk of injury to that child. Furthermore, cases provided notice that a defendant's failure to protect a child from harm created a situation that was violative of § 53-21(a)(1). Next, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant's failure to supervise his children adequately, despite his knowledge that the back door of his home was unsecured, amounted to a reckless disregard for a situation that was inimical to the physical welfare of his child. Finally, the trial court properly revoked defendant's probation. It considered his long criminal history in addition to his violation of § 53-21.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Thomas W.


AC 29003


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


115 Conn. App. 467; 974 A.2d 19; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 315


April 13, 2009, Argued 
June 30, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Thomas W., 294 Conn. 911, 983 A.2d 276, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 523 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Thomas W., 2011 Conn. LEXIS 283 (Conn., July 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and with the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, and tried to the jury before Scarpellino, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of one count of risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2); two counts of risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1); and one count of sexual assault in the fourth degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A) (Rev. to 2003).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from actions he took toward a six-year-old female, for whom he was a great uncle. Defendant regularly visited the victim's home and when the victim's mother was at work, allegedly performed a sexual act upon himself while in the kitchen. Shortly thereafter, defendant watched the victim while she used the bathroom. Further, in another incident, the victim stated that defendant touched her buttocks under her pajamas. On appeal, defendant claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1) was void for vagueness. However, the court held that the statute was not vague as applied to the circumstances of the case since it afforded defendant sufficient notice that performing a sex act in the kitchen where a six-year-old could observe him was prohibited by § 53-21(a)(1) as the statute prohibited wilfully creating a situation in which the morals of a minor were likely to be impaired. The court rejected defendant's argument that merely looking at the victim while she used the bathroom was prohibited conduct under the statute as such action, especially after the kitchen incident, threatened the victim's morality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

thereafter, the court, Winslow, J., issued an order modifying the respondents' visitation rights, and the petitioner appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Kahn, J., denied the respondents' motion for contempt, from which the respondents filed an amended appeal with the Supreme Court, which  [***2] transferred the appeal to this court; thereafter, the court, Bear, J., issued an order permitting the petitioner to withdraw her motion to suspend visitation as to one of the children, and the respondents appealed to this court.
In re Justin F. Hailee L., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3409 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 9, 2008)



DISPOSITION: In AC 29498, AC 29498-A01, AC 29498-A03, AC 29498-A04 and AC 30610, affirmed; appeals in AC 29498-A02, AC 29498-A05, AC 29498-A06, AC 30611 and AC 29912 dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, respondent pro se parents challenged multiple decisions of the trial court (Connecticut) relating to petitioner commissioner of children and families' efforts to terminate their parental relationship with two minor children and/or to reunited the parents with the children. The commissioner appealed from a court order granting unsupervised visitation to the parents.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner took custody of the children, who were adjudged neglected. One trial court found that the commissioner need not reunify the family because the parents were delusional. A subsequent trial court ordered the commissioner to facilitate reunification under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-129(b), (d), and (j) and provide parental visitation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-10a(a). On consolidated appeals of 10 different court orders, the court held, inter alia, that the parents offered no evidence in support of their motion to revoke the children's commitment. The trial court appropriately required the parents to take specific steps before unsupervised visitation and reunification could occur, including cooperating with the commissioner and visiting the children as often as the commissioner permitted. The trial court properly found that the commissioner was not in contempt of the visitation order because the parents bore the responsibility for failing to attend scheduled visitations. Based on a therapist's recommendation, the trial court properly ordered that the children not be forced to visit with their parents and properly transferred the case for a child protection hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed five of the trial court's orders concerning the children and dismissed the appeals of five other court orders for lack of jurisdiction based on mootness, including the commissioner's appeal.

Hummel v. Marten Transp., Ltd.


AC 28813, AC 30000


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


114 Conn. App. 822; 970 A.2d 835; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 221


January 8, 2009, Argued 
June 9, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hummel v. Marten Transp., Ltd., 293 Conn. 907, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 446 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal, in the first case, from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district ordering the named defendant to pay the plaintiff, inter alia, certain unpaid survivor benefits, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the award in part and remanded the case to the commissioner for further proceedings, and the defendants appealed to this court; appeal in the second case from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the fifth district, which, on remand from the workers' compensation review board, awarded the plaintiff attorney's fees and certain penalties for, inter alia, unpaid survivor benefits, brought to the workers' compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff filed a separate appeal to this court, which consolidated the appeals.
Hummel v. Marten Transp., Ltd., 282 Conn. 477, 923 A.2d 657, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 198 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an employer and its insurer, challenged decisions of the Workers' Compensation Review Board (Connecticut), which affirmed the Workers' Compensation Commissioner's finding that work-related stress was a substantial factor in an employee's death, awarded plaintiff widow a penalty under the Workers' Compensation Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-303, and refused to reduce her award by the amount of social security widow's benefits she received.


OVERVIEW: The employee was a cross-country truck driver. He was found dead in the sleeper cab of the employer's truck. An autopsy report established that the cause of death was ischemic heart disease. The widow filed a workers' compensation claim. The appellate court held that the evidence supported the Commissioner's finding with a reasonable medical probability that the stress of the employee's job and its limitations on his time for other activities was a substantial factor in the chain of events that precipitated his fatal disease. The Board correctly ruled that the plain meaning of the Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-301(f), provided no alternative to the payment of an award during the pendency of an appeal if the widow sought payment. Defendants' continuing refusal to compensate the widow for the compensable death of the employee was the type of behavior that § 31-303, by its terms, had to prevent. Defendants' request for a setoff was properly denied. The plain meaning of the Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-307(e) (Rev. to 1997), showed that was inapplicable to the widow's simultaneous collection of widow's benefits and social security widow's benefits under the Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-306.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decisions of the Board.

State v. Graves


AC 29905


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


114 Conn. App. 852; 971 A.2d 723; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 227


March 9, 2009, Argued 
June 9, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of reckless driving, failure to bring a motor vehicle to a full stop when signalled, reckless endangerment in the first degree, interfering with an officer, possession of marijuana and possession of marijuana with intent to sell, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number ten, where the court, Abrams, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of reckless driving, failure to bring a motor vehicle to a full stop when signalled, reckless endangerment in the first degree, interfering with an officer and possession of marijuana, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Graves, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1128 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 26, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) for, inter alia, reckless driving, reckless endangerment in the first degree, interfering with an officer, and possession of four ounces or more of a cannabis-type substance. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his pretrial motion to suppress evidence of a brown paper bag containing marijuana.


OVERVIEW: A Rhode Island police officer observed a car speeding. Defendant, who was the driver, stopped on a dirt road. After approaching the car, the officer observed a large, brown paper bag on the front passenger seat. The officer detected the odor of raw or bulk marijuana emanating from the vehicle. Defendant subsequently sped away and crossed the Connecticut state line. The officer pursued defendant. Other officers joined the pursuit. The officers proceeded to defendant's residence, parked and awaited the arrival of Connecticut authorities. After finding defendant's car, without the bag, the officer retraced the route of the pursuit and located the bag in an open field. The appellate court held the trial court properly determined that the officer was in hot pursuit of defendant at the time he searched defendant's property. The fact that the officer was a police officer from another state did not make his search in Connecticut per se unconstitutional. The search required neither a warrant nor an exception because it was conducted in an area, an open field, where defendant could not legitimately expect privacy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Richards


AC 28567


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


113 Conn. App. 823; 968 A.2d 920; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 153


October 28, 2008, Argued 
April 21, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Richards, 292 Conn. 905, 973 A.2d 107, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 327 (2009)
Appeal dismissed by, Review improvidently allowed by State v. Richards, 299 Conn. 238, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 460 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
(Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, Ginocchio, J. [motion to suppress]; Caroll, J. [judgment]).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) for possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle following his conditional plea of nolo contendere. He argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence that the police seized from an automobile that he was driving prior to an investigatory detention by the police of the automobile and its occupants.


OVERVIEW: At approximately 1:30 a.m., police officers observed a car being operated by defendant stop in a high drug area. The car had Vermont license plates, indicating it was potentially a rental car, a tactic used by drug dealers. A pedestrian approached the passenger side of the car and briefly conversed with the occupants before continuing on her way. She subsequently told the officers the occupants had asked her, using slang, if she was interested in purchasing drugs. The police stopped the car. The occupants moved around, turned their heads and ducked. An officer searched the passenger compartment and located a smaller compartment behind a child's car seat. The officer discovered a handgun. Defendant argued that the officers' brief conversation with the pedestrian, viewed in isolation, did not yield facts that supported a reasonable and articulable suspicion of criminal activity as there was no showing that the pedestrian was reliable. The appellate court rejected that argument and held there were many factors that constituted the totality of the circumstances known to the police to support an investigative stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with four counts each of the crimes of possession of a motor vehicle with an altered vehicle identification number and conspiracy to possess a motor vehicle with an altered vehicle identification number, and with the crimes of larceny in the first degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, forgery in the second degree and improper use of a motor vehicle registration, and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with five counts each of the crimes of possession of a motor vehicle with an altered vehicle identification number and conspiracy to possess a motor vehicle with an altered vehicle identification number, and two counts each of the crimes of larceny in the first degree, conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree and forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number twelve, and tried to the jury before Cofield, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a mistrial; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

OUTCOME: The appellate court, about the Corvette, reversed on one conspiracy to commit larceny count and three conspiracy to possess with altered VIN counts. As to the Escalade, it vacated convictions on three possession with altered VIN counts and four related conspiracy counts. As to the Navigator, it vacated as to one possession with altered VIN count and two related conspiracy counts. It also ordered corrected sentences and otherwise affirmed.

State v. Vilchel


AC 27000


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


112 Conn. App. 411; 963 A.2d 658; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 38


September 10, 2008, Argued 
February 3, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Vilchel, 291 Conn. 907, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 190 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit assault of public safety personnel, attempt to commit assault in the first degree, conspiracy to sell narcotics and sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the matter was tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a judgment of acquittal and for a new trial; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempt to commit assault of public safety personnel, attempt to commit assault in the first degree and conspiracy to sell narcotics, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Stat. §§ 53a-167c(a)(1) and 53a-49(a)(2). Defendant claimed that the trial court deprived him of his due process right to a fair trial by failing to instruct the jury to consider, inter alia, whether his conduct was justified in light of illegal conduct by the police.


OVERVIEW: Police officers entered defendant's residence in regard to a drug transaction, while wearing police badges. Defendant approached an officer while attempting to insert an ammunition clip into a pistol that he was pointing at the officer. The officer shot defendant. The instructions related to defendant's limited common-law privileges to resist certain types of unlawful police conduct were irrelevant to the issues actually before the jury and, thus, properly were omitted from the court's charge. The appellate court was not persuaded that any constitutional violation existed and rejected all aspects of defendant's claim. An instruction concerning the defense of renunciation was not warranted by the evidence presented.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Rose


AC 28174


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


112 Conn. App. 324; 963 A.2d 68; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 30


October 17, 2008, Argued 
January 27, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Rose, 290 Conn. 920, 966 A.2d 238, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 79 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Rose, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 277 (Conn., July 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of assault of public safety personnel, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Bellis, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Rose, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1786 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 15, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant, a pretrial detainee, guilty of assault of public safety personnel, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167c(a)(5). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict. Defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence and the requirement that he wear prison garb during the trial.


OVERVIEW: When defendant spat on an employee's face and chest, the jury could have found that defendant intended to assault the employee and to prevent him from performing his duties. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. However, the court found that the trial court improperly compelled defendant to wear prison garb at trial, in violation of his U.S. amend. VI and XIV, § 1, right to a fair and impartial trial. In order to protect the fair trial right and the presumption of innocence, a record had to be made establishing an essential state policy for the garb and shackles. If an interest was shown, jurors had to be instructed not to consider defendant's appearance when determining guilt or innocence. The potential prejudice was especially great because the jury had to find that defendant had the required mens rea. The intent evidence sufficed for a conviction but was not so overwhelming that there was no reasonable possibility that appearance might have contributed to the conviction. The State did not prove that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant did not receive a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Fontaine


AC 28566


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


112 Conn. App. 190; 962 A.2d 197; 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 16


October 10, 2008, Argued 
January 20, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Fontaine, 290 Conn. 921, 966 A.2d 238, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 69 (2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Fontaine, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 122 (Conn. App. Ct., Mar. 13, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crimes of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension and with improper visibility of reflectors, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, where the court, J. Fischer, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the charge of improper visibility of reflectors, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.
State v. Fontaine, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 538 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 9, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a and with operating a motor vehicle while his license was suspended under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-215. The State claimed a moped was a "motor vehicle."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was operating a moped with a motor of less than 50 cubic centimeters on a public highway. State police troopers observed him traveling at a speed of approximately 30 miles per hour. The moped was traveling in the right shoulder of the road and crossed over into the travel lane of the roadway several times. A trooper testified that there appeared to be a light attached to the rear of the moped, but the light was difficult to see as it was hanging loosely off the back of the moped. Defendant pulled into a parking lot. As a trooper spoke with defendant about the taillight being a public safety concern, he noticed that defendant had bloodshot eyes and an odor of alcohol on his breath. The trooper performed a series of field sobriety tests and placed defendant under arrest. The appellate court held that whether a vehicle was wholly self-propelled did not change whether it was a vehicle, and thus a motor vehicle, for the purposes of chapter 248. Per Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-212(5), any vehicle that was driven on the public highways was a motor vehicle under chapter 248. Thus, the moped was a motor vehicle for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-215 and 14-227a.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

State v. Osimanti


AC 28258


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 700; 962 A.2d 129; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 575


September 22, 2008, Argued 
December 23, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Osimanti, 290 Conn. 914, 965 A.2d 554, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 73 (2009)
Affirmed by State v. Osimanti, 299 Conn. 1, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 399 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for manslaughter by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut). Defendant claimed that the trial court denied him his constitutional and statutory rights to present relevant self-defense evidence, improperly instructed the jury on self-defense, failed to inquire adequately into alleged juror bias and improperly instructed the jury on reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed the victim with a box-cutter after an extended argument. Although the trial court limited defendant's cross-examination of a witness to events that occurred after a certain date, it admitted evidence that the victim had been convicted of threatening in the second degree, assault in the third degree four separate times, and assault in the second degree. The jury also heard testimony that the victim was in prison numerous times and was a member of a street gang. Further, defendant was able fully to cross-examine each witness who observed the confrontation and to present witnesses on his behalf to establish his self-defense claim. The appellate court held defendant's cross-examination of the witness was not unduly restricted and that the limitation imposed by the trial court did not infringe on defendant's confrontational and due process rights. The trial court's charge on defendant's duty to retreat that the charge complied with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-19(b) and (c). The trial did not abuse its discretion by the limited scope of its investigation of alleged juror bias and its conclusion regarding the absence of juror bias found adequate support in the record.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Wilson


AC 28554


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 614; 960 A.2d 1056; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 569


September 15, 2008, Argued 
December 16, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Wilson, 290 Conn. 917, 966 A.2d 234, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 92 (2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Wilson, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2787 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 28, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Wilson v. Warden, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 278 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics and possession of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Blawie, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of six crimes involving the sale and possession of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent within 1,500 feet of a school. Defendant was sentenced to a total term of 30 years imprisonment, execution suspended after 26 years, and five years probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from an undercover operation. Defendant asserted on appeal that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress the evidence seized during a search of his vehicle at the scene. The court disagreed and held that the warrantless search of his vehicle and the seizure of the items found within it was constitutionally valid pursuant to the automobile exception since the totality of the facts were sufficient to warrant a man of reasonable caution in the belief that more narcotics would be found in the vehicle based on defendant driving his vehicle to the scene and providing narcotics for all of the customers inside a restaurant, which indicated that he was in possession of a substantial quantity of narcotics that were not for his personal use. Further, the police finding narcotics in defendant's cellular telephone showed that he had even more narcotics to sell, thus, it was reasonable for the officers to infer that there was a fair probability he was storing even more narcotics in his vehicle. The court found that no prosecutorial misconduct occurred during closing argument, nor did the trial court err on instructing the jury on reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Spikes


AC 27547


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 543; 961 A.2d 426; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 561


May 29, 2008, Argued 
December 16, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Spikes, 290 Conn. 901, 967 A.2d 114, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 84 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Spikes v. Connecticut, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 5953 (U.S., Oct. 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit burglary in the second degree, burglary in the second degree and criminal mischief in the second degree and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree and larceny in second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Vitale, J., granted the state's motion to consolidate; thereafter the case was tried to the jury before Vitale, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed two judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of burglary in the third degree and larceny, with regard to a February 19, 2005 incident, and of attempt to commit burglary in the second degree, burglary in the second degree, and criminal mischief in the second degree based on a February 23, 2005 incident, following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from two separate incidents involving the same residence. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence supporting his convictions. The court found that, based on the evidence that defendant was seen in the vicinity of the burglarized home, the fact that he was found nearby with items of stolen jewelry on his person, and based on footprints in the snow matching his boots being found at the scene, there was sufficient evidence. The court found no merit to defendant's challenges to the value of the property provided at trial since the owners were competent to testify as to their opinion of the value of the jewelry stolen as well as provided their estimates of what the items were originally purchased for. Further, testimony from the owners' insurance agent as to the items of jewelry not recovered also was sufficient. The court found no merit to defendant's contention that the trial court erred by instructing the jury on the value of the property. The court further found no prosecutorial misconduct with regard to the prosecutor's closing argument and his comments that defendant failed to support his theory of innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

State v. Easton


AC 28652


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 538; 959 A.2d 1085; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 544


September 22, 2008, Argued 
December 9, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Easton, 290 Conn. 916, 965 A.2d 555, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 87 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, and tried to the court, Bellis, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk, Geographical Area Number Twenty, (Connecticut) that revoked his probation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32 and imposed the remainder of his sentence; defendant claimed that his due process rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conditions of probation included a general condition that he was not to violate any criminal laws. However, 25 days after his release, defendant was arrested for driving with a suspended license. An inventory search of his vehicle revealed 66.2 grams of marijuana. As a result, a warrant for his arrest for a violation of probation was issued pursuant to § 53a-32. Defendant claimed that by holding the probation and drug dependency hearings before a trial on the pending criminal charges, he was prevented from testifying and presenting a defense of his drug dependency, in violation of his Sixth Amendment right, and that instead he had to invoke his Fifth Amendment right to remain silent so as not to incriminate himself in his other pending matters. The appellate court found, inter alia, that after defendant was informed of his Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination, he conferred with his attorney and weighed his options. Thereafter, he chose not to present a defense as to his drug dependency, but rather to exercise his right of allocution. The fact that defendant had to make a difficult choice between two constitutional rights did not deprive him of due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

562 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aziegbemi


AC 28231


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 259; 959 A.2d 1; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 516


September 9, 2008, Argued 
November 18, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Aziegbemi, 290 Conn. 901, 962 A.2d 128, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 568 (Conn., Dec. 16, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, attempt to commit risk of injury to a child and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Hon. John F. Mulcahy, Jr., judge trial referee; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut), rendered after a jury trial, finding him guilty of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a)(2) and 53-21(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed (1) the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction under the "situation" prong of § 53-21(a)(1), and (2) § 53-21(a)(1) was unconstitutionally vague as applied in the case. The appeals court found defendant engaged the victim in flirtatious conversation, grabbed her wrist and neck, and attempted to pull her forcibly through his vehicle's open window. Pursuant to § 53-21(a)(1), ample evidence was offered from which the jury reasonably could have concluded that defendant had attempted to engage the victim in conduct that would result in injury to her physical well-being or mental health, or the impairment of her morals. A person of ordinary intelligence would have understood that this conduct constituted a substantial step in furtherance of the crime of attempt to commit risk of injury to a child. Defendant, by means of the common and legal meanings of "health," "impairment," and "morals," and through legal precedents, had fair warning that this conduct was violative of the situation prong of § 53-21(a)(1). Section 53-21(a)(1) provided fair notice and guidance to defendant sufficient to allow him to determine whether his conduct was permitted or prohibited.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

563 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Channy Nee Khuth


AC 28271


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


111 Conn. App. 184; 958 A.2d 218; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 507


September 24, 2008, Argued 
November 11, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Channy Nee Khuth, 289 Conn. 957, 961 A.2d 423, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 562 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Khuth v. Warden, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3430 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree as an accessory, and with the crimes of assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Schuman, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Khuth, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2282 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 24, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to suppress his statement was denied. A jury convicted defendant of first degree assault, first degree conspiracy to commit assault, and two counts of first degree assault as an accessory. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to a total effective term of 40 years, execution suspended after 30 years, with five years probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to suppress because defendant was under the influence of alcohol at the time police took his statement and thus, it was not voluntary. The appellate court found that defendant was not intoxicated, having last consumed alcohol more than 20 hours before giving the statement. In addition, defendant was familiar with his rights and voluntarily signed the waiver form. Defendant also argued that the trial court improperly failed to alleviate the jury's apparent confusion over the meaning of the word "aided" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59. The appellate court concluded that defendant waived any right to challenge the instruction when he specifically told the court that he agreed with the court's definition and that he did not want further instructions. Finally, defendant argued the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment of acquittal because the State failed to prove that he was aided by two or more persons. The appellate court disagreed, finding that there was sufficient evidence that one person's attack of a second victim aided defendant and that a second person acting as a lookout also aided defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Mitchell


AC 28998


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


110 Conn. App. 305; 955 A.2d 84; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 442


April 28, 2008, Argued 
September 16, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Mitchell, 289 Conn. 946, 959 A.2d 1012, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 512 (2008)
Related proceeding at State v. Hampton, 293 Conn. 435, 978 A.2d 1089, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 367 (2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Mitchell v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1726 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 26, 2013)
Motion for new trial denied by Mitchell v. State, 2016 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2258 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 22, 2016)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Certificate of appealability denied Mitchell v. Commmissioner of Corr., 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 153197 (D. Conn., Nov. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, conspiracy to commit murder, kidnapping in the first degree, conspiracy to commit kidnapping in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit sexual assault in the first degree, assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit assault in the first degree and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Mullarkey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) for, inter alia, attempt to commit murder. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court, sua sponte, should have declared a mistrial after witnesses testified about defendant's criminal history and prior arrests, that the prosecutor engaged in impropriety, and that the court improperly admitted a letter discussing escape plans.


OVERVIEW: During the trial, the victim made reference to defendant selling crack. The trial court struck the testimony and instructed the jury to disregard it. Defendant declined the trial court's offer of a curative instruction regarding another witness's testimony which made reference to defendant's criminal past. In declining the instruction, the defendant made a legitimate tactical decision not to emphasize the testimony. The trial court will not second-guess such decisions on appeal. The appellate court could not conclude that it was apparent to the trial court that the challenged testimony deprived defendant of a fair trial. Although the appellate court agreed that the prosecutor committed impropriety in mentioning certain specifics of defendant's prior felony conviction, it determined that defendant was not denied a fair trial. The trial court properly weighed the possible prejudice of the letter against its probative value. Not only did the court find that the letter was not more prejudicial than probative, but it also clearly instructed the jury that the letter did not raise a presumption of guilt and could be considered only as evidence that the defendant was conscious of guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Williams


AC 27941


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


110 Conn. App. 329; 954 A.2d 878; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 441


May 20, 2008, Argued 
September 16, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school and criminal possession of a firearm, and, in the second part, with being a persistent felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, D'Addabbo, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Williams, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1664 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of a school, and criminal possession of a firearm. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Police officers executed an arrest warrant for defendant at an apartment and found him sitting on a couch. Defendant was arrested. A detective removed the cushions from the couch and discovered a pistol. A sergeant noticed a box of ammunition. He conducted a protective sweep of the apartment and discovered narcotics on the kitchen counter. Defendant moved to suppress all tangible evidence recovered from him and the apartment. The trial court found that the contraband seized from the kitchen was discovered during a search incident to a lawful arrest. The appellate court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress. Once defendant was placed under arrest pursuant to a valid warrant, the sergeant properly conducted a search for any weapons or evidence within defendant's immediate control. It would not have been impossible for defendant to have reached items located in the area searched because the distance between the couch and the kitchen counter was six to eight feet. The fact that defendant was handcuffed did not foreclose the possibility that he could have been able to reach a weapon.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Carter v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 28712


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


109 Conn. App. 300; 950 A.2d 619; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 363


April 25, 2008, Argued 
July 22, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Fuger, J., rendered judgment dismissing the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Fuger, J., issued an articulation of its decision.
State v. Carter, 84 Conn. App. 263, 853 A.2d 565, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 335 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a second petition for a writ of habeas corpus, naming the Connecticut Commissioner of Correction as a party. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) dismissed his petition pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 23-29(3) as a successive petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: A jury found the inmate guilty of first degree assault, attempt to commit first degree assault, risk of injury to a child, and criminal possession of a firearm. He raised 14 claims in his first habeas petition, which was denied. He contended that the habeas court improperly dismissed his petition as a successive petition. The general grounds for relief in the second petition were the same as previously alleged: prosecutorial impropriety and ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court held that the record was inadequate to permit review of the inmate's claim that his second petition was based on new evidence. He did not offer any supporting facts as to why, with the exercise of due diligence, this evidence was not discoverable at time of the original petition, and he did not file a transcript of the relevant portions of his first habeas trial. Without a complete record, the appellate court was unable to determine whether the allegedly new evidence reasonably could have been incorporated into the inmate's original petition. Therefore, it declined to reach the merits of his claim.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Watrous v. Watrous


AC 28039, AC 28839


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


108 Conn. App. 813; 949 A.2d 557; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 334
