PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the defendant filed a cross complaint; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Swienton, J.; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion for a continuance; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the defendant appealed to this court; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for contempt, and the defendant filed a separate appeal to this court.
Watrous v. Watrous, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2276 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 26, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Dissolution judgment reversed in part; further proceedings; judgment of contempt affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New London Superior Court (Connecticut) in one case denied defendant husband's continuance motion, entered judgment dissolving his and plaintiff wife's marriage, ordered him to obtain medical and life insurance with the minor child and wife, respectively, as beneficiaries, and granted certain other relief. In a second case, it found him in contempt of its earlier orders. The husband appealed the rulings in both cases.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife married, had a minor daughter, and divorced. After a trial, a judgment of dissolution was rendered. The husband was ordered to pay to the wife certain weekly child support and alimony. It also ordered the husband to provide medical insurance and life insurance to them. The husband appealed. The wife then filed a motion for contempt in the trial court and alleged he had disobeyed the trial court's earlier order. After a hearing, the trial court found the husband in contempt and awarded the wife attorney fees. The husband appealed. The appellate court considered the two appeals and found that (1) as to the first appeal, the trial court erred in ordering the husband to obtain the insurance without having evidence as to its cost, (2) the trial court properly applied Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56(c)'s best interest factors in determining custody, (3) it properly denied his motion for continuance made the morning of trial after the case had been pending for almost two years, (4) as to the second appeal, the trial court's contempt finding was consistent with the contempt motion allegations, and (5) the husband did not show how the trial court was biased against him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court in the first case reversed the judgment as to the financial orders only and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings; otherwise the judgment was affirmed in all other respects. The appellate court in the second case affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Page v. State Marshal Comm'n


AC 27578


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


108 Conn. App. 668; 950 A.2d 529; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 330


February 19, 2008, Argued 
July 1, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Page v. State Marshal Comm'n, 289 Conn. 921, 958 A.2d 152, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 420 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to enjoin the defendant from implementing certain policies as to state marshals, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Tanzer, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Page v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 941 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state marshal sought to enjoin defendant state marshal commission from enforcing an on-call policy on grounds that it violated Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 6-38a, 6-38b(g); U.S. Const. amend. V, XIII, and XIV; and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 11. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) granted the commission's motion to dismiss on grounds of sovereign immunity. The marshal appealed.


OVERVIEW: Even though the complained-of policy was replaced by another policy that no longer required the marshal to appear at a courthouse in person, the court found that the appeal was not moot because the policy was subject to change at the discretion of the commission or the judicial branch and the main issue was whether the implementation of procedures under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-38b(g) violated the marshal's rights as an independent contractor. The court found that the marshal's claim did not fall under the second exception to the sovereign immunity doctrine because he failed to show that he had a constitutionally protected liberty or property interest. The marshal's claim that the commission exceeded its authority did not fall within the third exception. The commission had authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-38b(g), (k) to implement a policy to aid in its statutory responsibility to ensure the expeditious service of restraining orders. The marshal's complaint lacked any factual allegations that, if proven, reasonably would have supported his assertion that the commission acted in excess of its statutory authority in implementing the policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Garcia


AC 28453


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


108 Conn. App. 533; 949 A.2d 499; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 324


December 3, 2007, Argued 
June 24, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Garcia, 289 Conn. 916, 957 A.2d 880, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 456 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, possession of marijuana with intent to sell and possession of marijuana with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the matter was tried to the jury before Prescott, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions to preclude and to suppress certain evidence; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Garcia, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3267 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) denied defendant's motions to preclude and to suppress certain evidence and entered judgment on a jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of various narcotics crimes, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278, 21a-278a(b), and 21a-277. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion in limine to prevent the State from admitting into evidence the cash seized from his car because the cash was relevant to the crimes charged and it was not unduly prejudicial: (1) the cash did not tend to arouse the jury's emotion, hostility or sympathy; (2) it was germane to the charges; (3) evidence and counterproof did not consume an undue amount of time; and (4) defendant had reasonable grounds to anticipate the evidence. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress because (1) the scope of a search incident to the arrest of a car's driver included the passenger compartment, regardless of whether the arrestee could gain access to it: (2) the cash was recovered from the trunk pursuant to the standardized procedures of an inventory search; and (3) the cash seized constituted drug proceeds. Forfeiture of the cash to the state was authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-36a(c). Defendant was unemployed and offered no plausible explanation as to how the cash was obtained, the cash was found in a car being used in a drug transaction, and defendant was convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Gay


AC 27667


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


108 Conn. App. 211; 947 A.2d 428; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 275


March 18, 2008, Argued 
June 3, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Gay, 288 Conn. 913, 954 A.2d 186, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 342 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, possession of narcotics and possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school or day care center and substitute information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of interfering with an officer, assault of a public safety officer, engaging police in pursuit, reckless driving and operating a motor vehicle while his license was under suspension and with theft or illegal possession of motor vehicle number plates, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Holden, J., on a plea of guilty to assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs and assault of a public safety officer; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motions to withdraw his guilty pleas; judgments of guilty,  [***2] from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Gay, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 609 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 7, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty (Connecticut), rendered after the denial of his motions to withdraw his guilty pleas, convicting him of assault in the second degree with a motor vehicle, operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, and assault of a public safety officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court abused its discretion by denying his motions to withdraw his guilty pleas alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant argued that if counsel had effectively interviewed the victim and adequately investigated the scene of the accident, he could have pursued a causation defense for the assault charge. Defendant alleged that the victim grabbed the steering wheel and caused the accident. The appellate court found that counsel's investigation was adequate based on her testimony that she reviewed police and witness reports and spoke with defendant about the reports' contents and avenues of possible further investigation. Counsel also testified that she informed defendant that a causation defense was problematic because he would have to testify, subjecting him to cross-examination and exposure of his inconsistent statement to police after the accident that he did not remember what caused the accident. The appellate court also found no merit in defendant's claim that his guilty pleas were not knowingly entered into but were made because counsel led him to believe that by pleading guilty he would gain more time to hire a private attorney.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Clark


AC 28371


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


107 Conn. App. 819; 947 A.2d 351; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 239


February 15, 2008, Argued 
May 20, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Clark, 288 Conn. 916, 954 A.2d 187, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 343 (2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Clark, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 226 (Conn., June 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of drugs within 1500 feet of a school, sale of a controlled substance, illegal manufacture, distribution, sale, prescription or administration of a controlled substance within 1500 feet of a school, and operation of a drug factory, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, Scarpellino, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and the state's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with various drug-related crimes. He filed a motion to suppress, which the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant's car after receiving a tip that defendant was selling drugs. The court first held that under Conn. Const. art. I, § 7, a seizure had occurred. Officers blocked defendant's vehicle in a manner that was intended to restrict and had the effect of restricting his freedom of movement. The officers' actions in immediately exiting their vehicle and approaching defendant's vehicle while asking him to roll down his window and wearing marked shirts and badges demonstrated their authority in such a manner that a reasonable person would not have believed that he was free to leave. Next, under the totality of the circumstances, the seizure was not based on a reasonable and articulable suspicion under § 7 and the Fourth Amendment. The informant did not indicate that he had observed any illegal activity. There was no other indication of firsthand knowledge on the part of the informant, who did not demonstrate any knowledge of defendant's future behavior. When the officers saw the defendant several hours after the call from the informant, they did not witness any illegal activity. The only information they were able to corroborate was the identifying information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Petaway


AC 27088


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


107 Conn. App. 730; 946 A.2d 906; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 242


December 3, 2007, Argued 
May 20, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Petaway, 289 Conn. 926, 958 A.2d 162, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 426 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Judgment entered by Petaway v. Warden, State Prison, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3367 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 23, 2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Petaway v. Comm'r of Corr., 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 406 (Conn. App. Ct., Oct. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the defendant was presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a plea of guilty to the charge of robbery in the first degree; thereafter, the court denied in part the defendant's motion for disqualification and denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea; subsequently, the court, Gold, J., rendered judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Petaway, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 665 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 5, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) denied defendant's motions for disqualification and to withdraw his Alford plea and rendered judgment of guilty to the crimes of robbery and conspiracy to commit robbery. Defendant appealed, claiming that he should have been allowed to withdraw his plea after the trial court imposed a 24-hour house arrest condition and a no arrest condition as part of a Garvin agreement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been arrested and charged with robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4). The court found that the trial judge did not err in refusing to disqualify himself from adjudicating the motion to withdraw the plea. The judge's conduct would not have led a reasonable person to question his impartiality, and no relevant case law was cited to support a claim that the judge who presided over a plea pursuant to a Garvin agreement should not have presided over a motion to withdraw the plea. Raising defendant's bond after he was arrested on another charge was appropriate and did not indicate bias. The trial court's finding that defendant understood that a curfew condition was actually a 24-hour house arrest was not clearly erroneous, and the challenged no arrest condition was not invalid. Because defendant did not meet his burden under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 39-27, there was no abuse of discretion in denying the motion to withdraw his guilty plea as to the house arrest condition. An argument that the probable cause standard was improperly used to determine whether he breached the Garvin agreement was not supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Smith


AC 27837


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


107 Conn. App. 666; 946 A.2d 319; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 225


February 11, 2008, Argued 
May 13, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Smith, 288 Conn. 902, 952 A.2d 811, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 286 (Conn., June 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Prescott, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(3), kidnapping in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B), and sexual assault in the third degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(1). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to a total effective sentence of twenty-one years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress the pretrial and trial eyewitness identifications made by the victim because the identifications were the product of unnecessarily suggestive identification procedures in violation of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the photographic array, containing photographs that matched the description of the victim's attacker, from which the victim identified defendant did not create a very substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. Defendant's challenge to the admission of a chisel found in the victim's car failed as a chain of custody was established and the victim identified it as the same one she removed from her car. Next, the appellate court found no merit in defendant's claim of prosecutorial impropriety, noting that the prosecutor's arguments were based on facts in evidence and the reasonable inferences drawn from them. Finally, the court declined to address defendant's claim that the standard Chip Smith charge was unconstitutional, as the appellate court was bound by the precedent of the Connecticut Supreme Court upholding such an instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Carter v. Comm'r of Corr.

DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of assault, attempt to commit assault, risk of injury to a child, and criminal possession of a firearm, and was sentenced to a total effective term of 27 years of incarceration. The judgment was affirmed. The inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut). The inmate's petition for certification to appeal was denied.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed. The appellate court held that the inmate did not show that the habeas court abused its discretion in denying the petition for certification to appeal. To do so, the inmate had to demonstrate that the issues were debatable among jurists of reason, that a court could resolve the issues in a different manner, or that the questions were adequate to deserve encouragement to proceed further. After a careful review of the record and briefs, it was concluded that the inmate had not met that substantial burden.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Jarrett v. Comm'r of Corr.


AC 28297


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


106 Conn. App. 317; 942 A.2d 426; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 87


January 4, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
March 11, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Jarrett v. Comm'r of Corr., 287 Conn. 904, 947 A.2d 341, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 198 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, W. Sullivan, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Jarrett v. Barbieri, 1996 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1622 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 25, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven denied the petition. Defendant appealed. Defendant had claimed ineffective assistance of counsel for failure to prosecute the appeal. Defendant claimed that the habeas court improperly found there was no prejudice on his claim of an unconstitutional appellate delay.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The habeas court denied the petition as it found he had failed to meet his burden of proof as to ineffective assistance of counsel. The court granted the petition for certification to appeal. Defendant's counsel failed to file a timely appeal. Now, on appeal, defendant's only claim was that the habeas court should have permitted him to introduce evidence in support of his claim of appellate delay. The commissioner of the department of corrections objected to the attempt of defendant's counsel to offer evidence concerning appellate delay. The habeas court sustained the objection as it found that there was no prejudice. The appellate court held it was clear from the record that the habeas court understood that the delay had occurred but afforded the aspect of the Barker factors the appropriate weight because, in fact, defendant suffered no prejudice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court was affirmed.

State v. Smith


AC 28188


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


105 Conn. App. 278; 937 A.2d 1194; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 10


September 5, 2007, Argued 
January 15, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Smith, 286 Conn. 909, 944 A.2d 980, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 122 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, D'Addabbo, J., denied in part the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdicts and judgment of guilty on both parts of the information, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Smith, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1956 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 19, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and convicted him on a jury's verdict that found him guilty of robbery and kidnapping, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(3) and § 53a-92(a)(2)(B), respectively. Defendant's sentence was enhanced for being a persistent dangerous felony offender, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant's guest had common authority to consent to a warrantless entry into defendant's apartment because the guest had been staying there for a few weeks and others had come and gone while he was staying there. As a result, the officers were lawfully in a location where they could hear the ringing of a victim's cell phone, which was under a mattress, and the guest directed the officers' attention to a wastebasket where the victims' possessions were found. The guest's consent was not coerced. The one-on-one pretrial identification procedure was reliable because the victims identified defendant within two hours of the incident and they accurately described him before the challenged identification. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the guest's signed, prior inconsistent written statement into evidence for substantive purposes under the Whelan rule, even though the guest was found to be not credible, because credibility was grist for cross examination. Because the trial court, rather than the jury, made the requisite Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(h) public interest finding, defendant was entitled to a new sentencing proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction only as to the sentence imposed and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

State v. Robinson


AC 27282


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


105 Conn. App. 179; 937 A.2d 717; 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 7


September 6, 2007, Argued 
January 8, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Robinson, 286 Conn. 902, 943 A.2d 1102, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 146 (2008)
Affirmed by State v. Robinson, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 11 (Conn., Feb. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, possession of a hallucinogenic substance and possession of a hallucinogenic substance within 1500 feet of a school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number twenty, where the court, Dooley, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Jennings, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Robinson, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3676 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 6, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A substitute information charged defendant with violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(a), 21a-278a(b), 21a-279(b) and 21a-279(d). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) denied defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's warrantless arrest on property was lawful because the property was sufficiently enclosed, even with a small gateless entryway, to bring it within the protections of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-109(a)(1). The appellate court rejected defendant's Fourth Amendment argument that officers' search was only based on a hunch. There was more than ample evidence from which to form a reasonable and articulable suspicion that defendant was carrying contraband. There were prior reports of ongoing drug activity at the location. An officer recognized defendant and his companion from prior drug-related arrests. The officers saw defendant hide behind a wall and squat with his hand down the back of his pants, and they knew from past experience that drug dealers hid illegal drugs down their pants, between the cheeks of their buttocks, to evade detection. Defendant resisted an attempt to pat down the seat of his pants. Defendant's conduct during a properly conducted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-33k strip search was consistent with an attempt to hide contraband. The search was not a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-33l(b) body cavity search because there was no physical intrusion into defendant's anus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

578 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Valentin


AC 27187


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 805; 936 A.2d 662; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 446


October 18, 2007, Argued 
December 11, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Valentin, 285 Conn. 914, 943 A.2d 473, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 56 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, breach of the peace in the second degree, criminal trespass in the first degree and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, and tried to the jury before Shortall, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) convicted defendant of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, breach of the peace in the second degree, criminal trespass in the first degree, and interfering with an officer. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court declined to review defendant's unpreserved claim that the trial court improperly failed to instruct on self-defense with regard to the charge of attempted assault. In such a situation, to implicate a constitutional right, a defendant had to assert a claim of self-defense and present evidence to warrant a jury instruction on the defense. Here, defendant had not requested an instruction on self-defense, had not objected to the instruction given, and had not presented sufficient evidence to justify an instruction of self-defense. Thus, he had failed to demonstrate that his claim implicated a constitutional right. Next, defendant argued that the jury instruction regarding reasonable doubt was improper. Noting that this issue was also unpreserved for review, the court, reviewing the charge in its entirety, concluded that it was not reasonably possible that the instruction misled the jury. The trial court had stated, "The burden of proving the accused's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt requires the State to produce sufficient evidence to create in your minds a strong and abiding conviction of his guilt." The courts had upheld instructional language that was similar or identical.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

579 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lyon v. Jones


AC 27510


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 547; 935 A.2d 201; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 433; 102 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 665


October 5, 2007, Argued 
November 27, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Lyon v. Jones, 285 Conn. 914, 943 A.2d 472, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 58 (2008)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Lyon v. Jones, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 105 (Conn., May 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for alleged employment discrimination, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Keller, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the court, Stengel, J., granted the defendants' motion for judgment; subsequently, the court, Keller, J., rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Lyon v. Jones, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 595 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employee sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed her discrimination claims against defendants, the Office of the Attorney General as an employer and various employees, arising from the employee's termination from employment. She asserted claims of age, sex, and disability discrimination under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-60(a)(1) and 46a-70(a).


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an administrative complaint, alleging harassment, hostile work environment, and discrimination. The matter was released upon a finding of insufficient evidence of discrimination. The employee filed a federal action, which resulted in dismissals or summary judgment against her. The employee filed suit in a Connecticut court and defendants sought summary judgment. The trial court dismissed the claims, finding that the employee failed to obtain the requisite authorization prior to bringing the claims against the State. Further, the trial court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-99 provided her with a private right of action for injunctive relief. On appeal, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100 determined the applicable venue, but it did not constitute a waiver of the State's immunity. As the employee did not apply to the Claims Commissioner prior to bringing her claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-60(a)(1), the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. Dismissal of the claim under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-70(a) was also proper, as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-99 did not waive sovereign immunity for money damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Jenkins


AC 26833


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 417; 934 A.2d 281; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 418


May 21, 2007, Argued 
November 20, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part State v. Jenkins, 285 Conn. 909, 940 A.2d 809, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 37 (2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Jenkins, 298 Conn. 209, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 304 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Alexander, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Handy, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut), following his conditional plea of nolo contendere. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence because, inter alia, any consent to search a car was tainted by a prior, unconstitutional search of his person.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant make two illegal lane changes. The officer stopped the vehicle. After learning that defendant's license was valid and that there were no outstanding warrants, the officer nevertheless requested defendant's consent to search the car. The officer had defendant get out of the car and searched him even though the officer did not believe he was armed. After the officer did not find anything illegal on defendant's person, the officer asked defendant if he had anything illegal in the car. Defendant responded by stating that there was just some beer on the floor and to go ahead and check. The officer subsequently searched the entire car and found drugs. The appellate court concluded that defendant was unlawfully detained, that his consent to search the vehicle was tainted by that illegal detention and that the State failed to purge the taint of the illegal detention. Thus, the evidence procured through defendant's consent should have been suppressed. the record clearly revealed that the officer's inquiry into other suspected illegal activity came after his purpose for effectuating the stop had been achieved.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

State v. Marcial S.


AC 26479


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 361; 935 A.2d 154; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 411


September 11, 2007, Argued 
November 6, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Marcial S., 285 Conn. 907, 942 A.2d 415, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 19 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Salgado v. Warden, State Prison, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1528 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with three counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Blue, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for three counts of sexual assault in the first degree and two counts of risk of injury to a child. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly admitted hearsay evidence and constancy of accusation testimony, and improperly charged the jury on reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Beginning when the victim was approximately four years old, she periodically was sexually assaulted in her home by defendant, her father. According to the victim's testimony, the assaults took place sporadically and without any set pattern. Shortly after the first incident, the victim told her older sister about what had happened. The victim did not tell anybody else about the assaults until she was in the fourth grade, when she told a classmate. Later, in the sixth grade, the victim also told the classmate that she feared she was pregnant by her father. The classmate did not tell anybody about the victim's disclosures. Following the victim's birthday in sixth grade, she told another classmate about being molested. She then told her teacher. The appellate court held that the report of a licensed nurse practitioner was not improperly admitted as any evidence gathered at the clinic was incidental to the medical component of the examination. The classmate's testimony was admissible under the Troupe limitations to the constancy of accusation doctrine because it corroborated the timing of the victim's complaint. The jury instructions did not unconstitutionally reduce the State's burden.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

582 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Browne


AC 27662


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 314; 933 A.2d 735; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 414


March 26, 2007, Argued 
November 6, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected: January 10, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of marijuana with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a day care center, possession of more than four ounces of marijuana and possession of marijuana within 1500 feet of a day care center, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Holzberg, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of possession of more than four ounces of marijuana; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Superior Court, Judicial District of Middlesex, Connecticut, denied defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence, he entered a conditional plea of nolo contendere to possession of more than four ounces of marijuana. He then appealed.


OVERVIEW: The warrant application requested permission to search for cocaine, crack cocaine, and items related to the sale of narcotics, which it stated were believed to constitute evidence of possession of marijuana. The affidavit in support of the warrant application detailed the affiants' knowledge of defendant's involvement in the sale of marijuana, but the warrant itself named cocaine and crack cocaine, not marijuana, as an item to be seized. Police executed the warrant and seized several pounds of marijuana. The detective who prepared the application testified that cocaine was listed as an item to be seized because he had made a mistake when copying another warrant. The appellate court held that as the warrant did not describe the property sought, it was invalid. That the affidavit adequately described the "things to be seized" was immaterial, as the Fourth Amendment required particularity in the warrant, not in the supporting documents. The warrant did not incorporate other documents by reference, and was not accompanied by either the affidavit or the application. And as police were not lawfully on the premises where the marijuana was found, the plain view doctrine did not apply.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to grant defendant's motion to suppress.

State v. Skidd


AC 26678


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


104 Conn. App. 46; 932 A.2d 416; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 390


March 19, 2007, Argued 
September 25, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of intimidation based on bigotry or bias in the second degree and breach of the peace in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Wilson, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of intimidation based on bigotry or bias in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181k(a)(3) for threatening an individual while using a racial slur, and of breach of the peace in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181(a)(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from his attendance at a flea market. The victim was a neighbor to the parking lot where the flea market was held. The victim approached a woman and asked her not to dump her garbage. The victim called the police to report the dumping and, as he approached the parking lot again, defendant called him a foul name, used a racial slur, and made a gesture with his hands to indicate he wanted the victim to engage in a fight. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-181k(a)(3) on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad on its face and unconstitutionally vague as applied to him. The court held that § 53a-181k(a)(3) was not overbroad as it only criminalized true threats. Further, defendant's words and actions constituted an indication that something was impending, namely, a physical confrontation, and a person of ordinary intelligence would readily comprehend that defendant's actions were prohibited by § 53a-181k(a)(3), therefore, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant. The court found no merit in any of the evidentiary errors alleged by defendant on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

584 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Accident & Indem. Co. v. Ace Am. Reinsurance Co.


AC 25661


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


103 Conn. App. 319; 930 A.2d 701; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 340


May 30, 2007, Argued 
August 14, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Motion granted by Hartford Accident & Indem. Co. v. ACE Am. Reinsurance Co., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2470 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for breach of certain reinsurance contracts, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and transferred to the Complex Litigation Docket, where the court, Schuman, J., denied the plaintiffs' motion to compel the defendant underwriters of Lloyd's of London et al. to post security sufficient to secure any final judgment that may be rendered against them or, alternatively, to strike their answer and special defenses, and the plaintiffs appealed to this court, which granted the motion to dismiss filed by the defendant underwriters of Lloyd's of London et al., and the plaintiffs, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Supreme Court; thereafter, the Supreme Court reversed the judgment of this court and remanded the case to this court for further proceedings.
Hartford Accident & Indem. Co. v. ACE Am. Reinsurance Co., 279 Conn. 220, 901 A.2d 1164, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 277 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an insurance company and its affiliates, filed an action against defendant reinsurance companies for breach of various reinsurance contracts. Plaintiffs filed a motion under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-27 to either compel the posting of prepleading security or to strike defendants' answer and special defenses. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) denied the motion. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: In accordance with the reinsurance contracts, some defendants were served through agents rather than through substituted service. The court stated that as a remedial statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-27 was to be liberally construed. In light of the repeated references in the statute to other sections of Conn. Gen. Stat. tit. 38a, the court was not persuaded that the statute was meant to provide the remedy of prepleading security only if an unauthorized insurer was served through substituted service. It would be illogical to debar a plaintiff from this remedy because it had used a method of service authorized by contract. Next, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-271(c), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-27 did not apply to transactions involving industrial insureds. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-271(c), however, categorically prevented any part of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 38a-271 to 38a-278 from being applied to reinsurance contracts. Finally, if Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-27 were read literally to deny defendants a hearing on the amount of security they had to post, this would violate due process under the Fourteenth Amendment. Thus, defendants were entitled to a hearing on this issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment. It remanded the case for a determination of the appropriate amount of prepleading security, a question on which both parties would be entitled to present evidence.

 

585 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vollemans v. Town of Wallingford


AC 27332


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


103 Conn. App. 188; 928 A.2d 586; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 343; 101 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1020


January 12, 2007, Argued 
August 14, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Vollemans v. Town of Wallingford, 284 Conn. 920, 933 A.2d 722, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 442 (2007)
Affirmed by Vollemans v. Town of Wallingford, 289 Conn. 57, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 386 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for age discrimination, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven at Meriden, where the court, Tanzer, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
Vollemans v. Town of Wallingford, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 41 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 10, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former employee, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven at Meriden (Connecticut), which granted defendant employer's motion for summary judgment and thereby dismissed plaintiff's suit seeking to recover damages for age discrimination.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a superintendent at defendant's power plant. Defendant, a town, informed plaintiff that the plant was closing and his position was eliminated. Defendant retained plaintiff after the plant was decommissioned and plaintiff's counsel sent a letter advising that all of the employees of the plant being retained were much younger than plaintiff and that he was prepared to filed a complaint with the Connecticut Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities. Defendant terminated plaintiff in response. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendant upon determining that no genuine issues of material fact existed regarding defendant's claims that plaintiff's complaint was untimely filed with the Commission. The court determined, noting that the case was of first impression, that the time limit of 180 days set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-82(e) was mandatory and that, because plaintiff filed his complaint within 180 days from the final day of his employment, the complaint was timely filed. The court further found that plaintiff established a prima facie case of discrimination by showing that he was the oldest power plant employee and the only one retained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of defendant and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

586 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fennelly v. Norton


AC 27132


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


103 Conn. App. 125; 931 A.2d 269; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 326


March 20, 2007, Argued 
August 7, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Fennelly v. Norton, 284 Conn. 918, 931 A.2d 936, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 426 (2007)
Costs and fees proceeding at Fennelly v. Norton, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3212 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Application for visitation rights with the defendant's minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Burke, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, grandparents, filed an application for visitation with their grandchildren. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted a motion to dismiss by defendant. The grandparents appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents' application for visitation consisted solely of a standard custody-visitation application form on which they listed the name and date of birth of each minor child and checked four boxes. The application contained no specific factual allegations. The appellate court held that when faced with a motion to dismiss an application for visitation, the trial court was required under the Roth doctrine to scrutinize the application and to determine whether it contained specific, good faith allegations of both relationship and harm. The application for visitation contained no specific allegations of either the requisite relationship or harm. The mere act of checking a box on the application for visitation form that provided that the applicant had a relationship with the children that was similar in nature to a parent-child relationship and denial of visitation would cause real and significant harm to the children does not suffice for the specific, good faith allegations required. Furthermore, under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 25-4, it was incumbent on the grandparents to state the facts that supported their conclusions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pauling


AC 26973


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


102 Conn. App. 556; 925 A.2d 1200; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 296


March 21, 2007, Argued 
July 17, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Pauling, 284 Conn. 924, 933 A.2d 727, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 469 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of unlawful restraint in the first degree, assault in the second degree, failure to appear in the second degree and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Comerford, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal; verdict and judgment of guilty of unlawful restraint in the first degree, failure to appear in the second degree, failure to appear in the first degree and the lesser included offense of assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fairfield Superior Court (Connecticut) denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of unlawful restraint in the first degree, assault in the third degree, failure to appear in the second degree, and failure to appear in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim were involved in a romantic relationship. However, the relationship began to deteriorate. Even so, the victim allowed defendant to move into her apartment. When the victim seemed to be ignoring defendant, he became angry; as she tried to walk out of the bedroom where they were talking, he grabbed her by the hair and slapped her across the face. After he slapped her two more times, she hit him. She then scratched him. At least three times she got off the bed, but he grabbed her, and threw her back on the bed and continued to choke her. Eventually, defendant punched her twice in the face and kicked her. One of the punches caused her eyeball to go back into her socket. Defendant was later charged with criminal offenses and twice failed to show up in court. Following a jury trial, he was convicted of unlawful restraint in the first degree, assault in the third degree, failure to appear in the second degree, and failure to appear in the first degree. On appeal, the state supreme court found that the evidence supported the convictions, the State disproved his self-defense claim, and the jury was properly instructed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Fauntleroy


AC 27016


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


101 Conn. App. 144; 921 A.2d 622; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 186


February 15, 2007, Argued  
May 8, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit burglary in the third degree, criminal mischief in the third degree and attempt to commit larceny in the sixth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, and tried to the jury before Rodriguez, J.; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction, rendered in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) after a jury trial, for attempt to commit burglary in the third degree, criminal mischief in the third degree, and attempt to commit larceny in the sixth degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sufficiency of the evidence claims failed. The jury reasonably could have inferred from defendant's conduct, which included peering through the windows of a vehicle during the early morning hours in a well lit parking lot, pulling on the door frames and then striking the window with an object, that defendant had seen coats in the back of the vehicle and intended to steal the coats when he broke the window. Also, a witness, who had been in rightful possession of the vehicle prior to, during and following the incident, testified that defendant did not have her consent to enter the vehicle. Defendant's claim that the superior court improperly instructed the jury on an essential element of larceny in the sixth degree failed. The superior court's charge, when read as a whole, did not mislead the jury by relieving the state of its burden of proving all of the essential elements of the crime charged beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant's constitutional challenges to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-125b(a) and 53a-121(a)(3) were briefed inadequately, and the court declined to review them.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

590 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adgers


AC 26408


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


101 Conn. App. 123; 921 A.2d 122; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 184


February 23, 2007, Argued  
May 8, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Adgers, 283 Conn. 903, 927 A.2d 915, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 310 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with nine counts of the crime of harassment in the second degree and, in the second part, with being a persistent offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Keller, J.; verdict of guilty of eight counts of harassment in the second degree; thereafter, the second part of the information was tried to the jury; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Adgers-Martinez v. State, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 315 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence upon which a jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, convicted him on eight of nine counts of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a)(2) harassment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sent letters to the victim, ostensibly civil pleadings, while he was in prison for the kidnapping and physically and sexually assaulting the victim. The civil suit against the victim was filed from prison. Defendant argued that because the mailings concerned civil pleadings, the state failed to establish that they would cause annoyance or alarm to a person of common intelligence. The appellate court affirmed. While a common-law privilege generally attached to legal pleadings, defendant implicitly acknowledged that the mailings were not privileged if the jury could reasonably find that they contained collateral notations that would cause the victim annoyance or alarm in light of the underlying history between the parties. All of the mailings contained such collateral notations. Defendant's alternative claim that § 53a-183 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to him also failed. Defendant could not reasonably infer from the victim's failure to object to the civil pleadings that she would not likely be alarmed or annoyed by the extraneous comments attached to the mailings. Further, the fact that § 53a-183 was a specific intent statute purged it of any potential vagueness.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

591 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hicks


AC 26878


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


101 Conn. App. 16; 919 A.2d 1052; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 192


October 25, 2006, Argued  
May 1, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and with the crime of burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Cofield, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Hicks v. Warden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 191 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him, following a jury trial, of burglary in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(2), assault in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and assault in the first degree, a violation of § 53a-59(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: None of defendant's claims were preserved at trial, and he sought to prevail under Connecticut v. Golding. The state appellate court affirmed. His claims that he was arrested without probable cause and that the "show-up" identification procedure was unduly suggestive were not reviewable because, while they were of a constitutional magnitude, the record was inadequate. The trial court made no factual findings or came to any legal conclusions respecting those claims. Further, defendant could not prevail on his claim that there was insufficient evidence to convict under § 53a-59(a)(4) as he misconstrued the application of § 53a-59(a)(4) to an accessory through Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-8. Convicting defendant as an accessory to assault was not to construe him as the "he" who actually inflicted hands-on injury while simultaneously construing the actual assailant to be a non-hands-on aider. Rather, defendant was punished as if he was the principal offender as his intent and willing assistance made him as culpable as the principal. Thus, one who was an aider for the purpose of establishing an element of the crime could also be liable as an accessory for giving such aid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Martin


AC 27112


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 742; 919 A.2d 508; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 167


January 3, 2007, Argued  
April 24, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 22, 2007.
Appeal denied by State v. Martin, 282 Conn. 928, 926 A.2d 667, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 282 (2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Martin v. Warden, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 322 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of felony murder, robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before White, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed; subsequently, this court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Richards, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Martin, 77 Conn. App. 818, 827 A.2d 1, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 290 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction entered, after a retrial, by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) convicting him of conspiracy to commit robbery, robbery, and felony murder, and sentencing him to an effective term of 75 years of incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his constitutional rights were violated by allowing the prior testimony of his brother to be entered into evidence. The appellate court considered the claim under Golding. Defendant's brother testified at the first trial, but refused to testify at the retrial. It was unclear whether the brother could assert his Fifth Amendment privilege as he had been sentenced for his participation in the crime. Thus, the brother was found to be unavailable for Confrontation Clause purposes based on his refusal to answer any questions presented to him, which satisfied the unavailability requirement. It was not plain error to fail to instruct the jury, sua sponte, on the affirmative defense to felony murder outlined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c. There was evidence that defendant had reasonable grounds to believe that co-defendant was armed with a gun moments before entering the store. Finally, the jury was not improperly instructed on reasonable doubt as it was not reasonably possible for it to have been misled. The invitation to reject precedent from the state's highest court and to adopt the cumulative error standard used by the federal courts was declined.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Edwards


AC 27113


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 565; 918 A.2d 1008; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 158


October 18, 2006, Argued  
April 17, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As corrected Sept. 5 2007.
Appeal denied by State v. Edwards, 282 Conn. 928, 926 A.2d 666, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 278 (2007)
Appeal denied by State v. Edwards, 282 Conn. 929, 926 A.2d 667, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 279 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of multiple offenses arising from four consolidated cases, including various types of murder and robbery. The trial court had denied defendant's acquittal motion. After merging various convictions, defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without release plus an additional term.


OVERVIEW: In four separate incidents, defendant robbed two victims at gunpoint and took their vehicles, he fatally shot two other victims upon attempting to rob them, and he failed to stop for police. The charges were consolidated and a jury trial resulted in convictions and sentences. On appeal, the court found sufficient evidence to support the convictions with respect to defendant's identity and the operability of the gun as to the two robberies. Defendant's assertion of his right to waive counsel was not knowing, intelligent, and voluntary pursuant to questioning under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 44-3, such that denial was proper. He was not unconstitutionally precluded from testifying in his own defense. The convictions for felony murder were properly based on the underlying offense of attempted robbery pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 42-29 (formerly § 867) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-60. Defendant's double jeopardy rights were violated where he was sentenced for the felony murders and the capital felony, and for the larceny and retention of a vehicle. There was no separate offense under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136a, as it was merely a sentence enhancement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter to the extent of directing a combination of the two felony murder convictions with the capital felony, a vacatur of the sentences for the felony murder convictions and for the larceny by retention of stolen property, and a vacatur of the conviction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136a. The remainder of the trial court judgment was affirmed.

State v. Owens


AC 26670


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 619; 918 A.2d 1041; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 161


October 23, 2006, Argued  
April 17, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Owens, 282 Conn. 927, 926 A.2d 668, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 272 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), for attempt to commit murder and risk of injury to a child. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly instructed the jury as to intoxication, failed to conduct an adequate inquiry as to juror misconduct, and improperly instructed the jury regarding attempt to commit murder and reckless assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant became upset when one of the victims told defendant she would not be able to take care of his daughter any longer. After drinking, defendant returned to the victim's house, argued with her, struck her, causing her to lose consciousness, and stabbed her. He "chased" the victim's 12-year-old daughter by running two or three steps toward her with a knife causing her to retreat to her bedroom. Approximately 25 minutes after having left the victims' house, defendant went to a police department and announced that he had just killed someone. The trial court gave an instruction on intoxication as framed by defendant. Thus, the appellate court held that defendant was precluded from claiming that the jury was improperly instructed as to intoxication. Even if there was error, it was induced. The trial court conducted a sufficient Brown hearing as to jury misconduct and defendant failed to demonstrate any prejudice. Contrary to defendant's assertions, the record reflected that the trial court did not emphasize the importance of the count asserting attempt to commit murder or minimize the importance of the count asserting reckless assault in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Maskiell


AC 26387


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 507; 918 A.2d 293; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 132


September 14, 2006, Argued  
April 10, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Maskiell, 282 Conn. 922, 925 A.2d 1104, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 254 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought to extend respondent acquittee's commitment to the psychiatric security review board. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Windham at Danielson (Connecticut) granted the acquittee's motion to open the judgment and denied his motion to dismiss. The acquittee appealed, claiming, inter alia, that the admission of the board's report violated his procedural due process and the evidence did not support the court's findings.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee was charged with the crimes of sexual assault in the fourth degree and risk of injury to a child. He was acquitted by reason of mental disease or defect pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-13. He was committed to the jurisdiction of the board. On subsequent occasions, the court granted the State's petitions for an order of continued commitment. The State filed a petition for an order for the acquittee's continued confinement. The board recommended that commitment be extended for a period of time not to exceed five years. The court granted the State's petition. The appellate court held the trial court was well within its authority to accept as true the prosecutor's representations concerning the existence of an agreement as to the admissibility of the board's report. Having effectively stipulated that the court properly could admit and consider the report, the acquittee induced the conduct that he challenged on appeal and was thus precluded from raising such claim under the doctrine of induced error. There was ample evidence to support the finding that the acquittee posed a significant danger to children as a result of his pedophilia.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Smith


AC 27136


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 313; 917 A.2d 1017; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 127


January 12, 2007, Argued  
April 3, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Smith, 282 Conn. 920, 925 A.2d 1102, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 238 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.  [***1]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found to be competent to stand trial. He was convicted by the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), of robbery larceny, and carrying a dangerous weapon. Before sentencing, defendant moved for a psychiatric examination pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-566. Defendant was found to be incompetent, but then was found to have been restored to competency. Defendant was sentenced. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that an inadequate canvass was conducted to ensure that his waiver of his right to a jury trial was knowing, voluntary, and intelligent. The appellate court held that as defendant had been found to be competent to stand trial, he was competent to waive his right to a jury trial under the Federal Constitution. Between the time of the competency hearing and the trial, neither party raised any concerns about defendant's competency. When defendant waived his right to a jury trial, defense counsel stated that the waiver was against the advice of counsel, but did not raise defendant's competence to make such a waiver. The trial court recollected that defendant's behavior had been ordinary and that he had testified in a coherent manner. He was also familiar with the court system, had received a general equivalency diploma while incarcerated, and was represented by, and conferred with, counsel. Finally, the Connecticut Supreme Court had rejected defendant's claim that the canvass was inadequate under the State Constitution as he was not apprised of certain rights provided under Conn. Const. art. I, § 19 that were not afforded under the Federal Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Payne


AC 26782


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


100 Conn. App. 13; 917 A.2d 43; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 91


January 3, 2007, Argued  
March 13, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Payne, 282 Conn. 914, 924 A.2d 139, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 223 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, Cofield, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of identity theft, forgery in the second degree, attempt to commit larceny in the second degree and criminal impersonation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen, where the court, Cofield, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
Payne v. TK Auto Wholesalers, 98 Conn. App. 533, 911 A.2d 747, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 495 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number seventeen (Connecticut), convicted defendant of identity theft, second-degree forgery, attempt to commit second-degree larceny, and criminal impersonation, after denying his motion to dismiss said charges. Defendant thus appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court improperly: (1) denied his motion for dismissal and request for an evidentiary hearing, based on his claim of selective prosecution, and (2) allowed evidence of his prior bad acts. The appeals court disagreed. First, defendant failed to make a prima facie showing with regard to either prong of the selective prosecution test, and, as such, he was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing or a dismissal. Moreover, nothing in defendant's offer of proof indicated that he could have proven that his claimed "suspect classification" as a "converter of property" was an impermissible consideration for prosecution, which would be necessary to satisfy prong two of the selective prosecution test. Second, even if the State initially had sought to introduce evidence of some bad acts related to a police stop, it did not elicit such testimony or make any representations that defendant engaged in anything improper relating to this stop. Further, the defendant denied having been stopped. Hence, the court failed to see how these questions resulted in evidence of prior bad acts or how they were prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

599 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


36 DeForest Ave., LLC v. Creadore


(AC 26573)


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


99 Conn. App. 690; 915 A.2d 916; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 75


November 14, 2006, Argued  
February 27, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by 36 Deforest Ave., LLC v. Creadore, 282 Conn. 905, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 181 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Fairfield, Radcliffe, J.) Application for discharge or reduction of a mechanic's lien filed against certain of the plaintiff's real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Radcliffe, J.; judgment denying the application, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.
36 DeForest Ave., LLC v. Creadore, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1298 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 6, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), denied an application by plaintiff, a limited liability company, for discharge or reduction of a mechanic's lien filed against certain of the company's real property by defendant. The company appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property was sold to the company by the daughter of a decedent. Prior to the decedent's death, the decedent and defendant had undertaken a number of improvements to the property. Defendant's lien was intended to secure payment for a portion of this work. The company argued that the lien was untimely, and that there was therefore no probable cause to sustain its validity. The appellate court held that the evidence presented, including defendant's testimony, his possession of keys to the premises, and a drawing that depicted work yet to be done, provided more than adequate support for the trial court's finding that the renovation project was ongoing at the time of the decedent's death. Thus, for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-34(1), the filing of the lien more than 90 days after the performance of some of the services did not compel a conclusion that the lien was untimely. The appellate court further held that service of the lien was proper, because "owner," as used in Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 49-34 and 49-35, meant only the owner at the time of service of the certificate of lien, and thus defendant was not required to serve the lien on the decedent's daughter.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Strich


AC 27371


APPELLATE COURT OF CONNECTICUT


99 Conn. App. 611; 915 A.2d 891; 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 65


November 15, 2006-, Argued  
February 20, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Strich, 282 Conn. 907, 920 A.2d 310, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 186 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Strich v. Conn., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 10096 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] (Appeal from Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, Cremins, J.) Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of assault in the first degree and burglary in the first degree and with the crimes of attempt to commit murder, criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, carrying a pistol without a permit and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the court, Cremins, J., granted the state's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of assault in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, attempt to commit murder, criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, carrying a pistol without a permit and possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of attempt to commit murder, assault in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, criminal possession of a pistol or revolver, carrying a pistol without a permit, and possession of weapons in a motor vehicle. The Superior Court, judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) imposed a total effective sentence of 40 years incarceration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court deprived him of his constitutional right to a fair trial by responding inappropriately to his disruptive courtroom behavior and limiting his opportunity to present evidence of his mental state. The appellate court disagreed, noting that, inter alia, the trial court warned defendant on numerous occasions that he would be removed from the courtroom if he continued disrupt the proceedings. The court did not order defendant's removal until the beginning of the prosecutor's closing argument. Thereafter, defendant was able to hear the proceedings in a holding cell. The appellate court further concluded that defendant's ex-wife would not have been a competent witness for testimony related to defendant's intent and that it was not error for the trial court to restrict defendant's cross-examination of her about an action she allegedly filed to recover damages for negligence in a hospital's psychiatric care of defendant. The appellate court also held that the trial court did not exceed its authority by issuing a restraining order for the protection of the victim's sister her former husband because the victim lived with them at the time of the assault.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
